(Psalms 1:1) 
Truly blessed is the man who does not follow the advice of the ungodly, nor stands in the path of sinners, nor sits in the seat of those who mock or spread moral corruption.

(Psalms 1:2) 
Instead, his deepest desire is found in the Law of the Lord, and he ponders over His Law both day and night.

(Psalms 1:3) 
Such a one will be like a tree planted by flowing streams of water, which yields its fruit in its proper season. Its leaves will not wither, and everything he undertakes will truly prosper.

(Psalms 1:4) 
The ungodly are not like this; they are certainly not! Instead, they are like the chaff which the wind drives away from the surface of the earth.

(Psalms 1:5) 
For this reason, the ungodly will not be able to stand righteous in the great judgment, nor will sinners be found among the assembly of the truly just.

(Psalms 1:6) 
Because the Lord intimately knows and approves the path taken by the just, but the way of the ungodly will utterly perish and lead to destruction.

(Psalms 1:7) 
Why have the nations risen in tumult, and why do the peoples devise futile plans?

(Psalms 1:8) 
The kings of the earth take their stand, and the rulers have gathered together against the Lord and against His Anointed One, the Christ.

(Psalms 1:9) 
They say: 'Let us break their bonds and throw off their yoke from us!'

(Psalms 1:10) 
The One enthroned above and beyond creation will laugh at them, and the Lord will utterly mock them.

(Psalms 1:11) 
Then He will speak to them in His anger, and in His burning wrath He will terrify them.

(Psalms 1:12) 
Yet I have been appointed King by Him over Sion, His holy mountain, proclaiming His decree.

(Psalms 1:13) 
The Lord has said to me: 'You are my Son; this very day I have begotten you.'

(Psalms 1:14) 
'Ask of Me, and I will give you the nations as your inheritance, and the very ends of the earth as your possession.'

(Psalms 1:15) 
'You will rule them with a rod of iron, and you will shatter them like a potter's vessel.'

(Psalms 1:16) 
And now, you kings, be wise; take instruction, you who govern the earth.

(Psalms 1:17) 
Serve the Lord with reverent fear, and rejoice in Him with trembling awe.

(Psalms 1:18) 
Embrace His discipline and teaching, lest the Lord become angry and you perish from the just path.

(Psalms 1:19) 
When His wrath flares up suddenly and for a short time, truly blessed are all who trust in Him.

(Psalms 1:20) 
O Lord, why have my tormentors multiplied? Many rise up against me!

(Psalms 1:21) 
Many are saying to my very soul: 'There is no salvation for him in his God!'

(Psalms 1:22) 
But You, O Lord, are my protector, my glory, and the One who lifts up my head.

(Psalms 1:23) 
With my voice, I cried out to the Lord, and He heard me from His holy mountain.

(Psalms 1:24) 
I lay down and slept deeply, and I awoke again, because the Lord sustained me.

(Psalms 1:25) 
I will not fear the thousands of people who surround me. Rise up, O Lord; save me, O my God!

(Psalms 1:26) 
For You have struck all those who opposed me without just cause; You have broken the teeth of the wicked sinners.

(Psalms 1:27) 
Salvation comes from the Lord, and Your blessing rests upon Your people.

(Psalms 1:28) 
For the End, or for the director of music, to be accompanied by stringed instruments. A Psalm of David.

(Psalms 1:29) 
When I called upon Him, the God of my righteousness heard me. In my tribulation, You gave me room to breathe. Have mercy on me, and hear my prayer.

(Psalms 1:30) 
O sons of men, how long will your hearts be heavy with sorrow and stubbornness? Why do you love what is vain and seek what is false?

(Psalms 1:31) 
And know this: the Lord has shown His holy one a wondrous favor. The Lord will hear me when I cry out to Him.

(Psalms 1:32) 
Be angry, but do not sin. Reflect on what you speak in your hearts, and in your silent chambers, be contrite.

(Psalms 1:33) 
Offer the sacrifice of righteousness, and place your hope in the Lord.

(Psalms 1:34) 
Many are asking: 'Who will show us good things?' The light of Your face, O Lord, has been impressed upon us as a sign.

(Psalms 1:35) 
You have given joy to my heart, more than they have from the abundance of their grain, wine, and oil.

(Psalms 1:36) 
For the End, or for the director of music, concerning the one who obtains the inheritance (possibly referring to a liturgical melody or the Church). A Psalm of David.

(Psalms 1:37) 
Lord, perceive my words with Your ears; understand my cry.

(Psalms 1:38) 
Attend to the voice of my prayer, O my King and my God, because it is to You alone that I will pray.

(Psalms 1:39) 
O Lord, in the morning You will hear my voice. In the morning, I will stand ready before You and look for Your answer.

(Psalms 1:40) 
For You are not a God who desires iniquity.

(Psalms 2:1) 
Why do the nations rage, and the peoples devise useless schemes?

(Psalms 2:2) 
The kings of the earth have taken their stand, and its rulers have assembled together against the Lord and against His Anointed King.

(Psalms 2:3) 
(The rebellious kings say,) "Let us break their chains, and let us cast off their yoke from us!"

(Psalms 2:4) 
He who sits enthroned in the highest heavens will laugh at them, and the Lord will mock them.

(Psalms 2:5) 
Then He will speak to them in His anger, and in His burning rage He will terrify them.

(Psalms 2:6) 
But I have established My King upon Zion, My holy mountain, and I will now declare My decree concerning Him.

(Psalms 2:7) 
The Lord said to me, "You are My Son. Today I have begotten you and declared your divine Sonship."

(Psalms 2:8) 
Ask of Me, and I will give you the nations as your inheritance, and the ends of the earth as your possession.

(Psalms 2:9) 
You shall rule them with an iron scepter, and shatter them like a potter's vessel.

(Psalms 2:10) 
Therefore, now, O kings, be wise; be instructed, you who govern the earth.

(Psalms 2:11) 
Serve the Lord with reverence, and rejoice in Him with awe and trembling.

(Psalms 2:12) 
Embrace His instruction, lest the Lord become angry, and you perish from the righteous path. For when His wrath is quickly kindled, blessed are all who trust in Him.

(Psalms 3:1) 
This Psalm by David was written when he fled from his own son, Absalom.

(Psalms 3:2) 
Oh Lord, why have those who trouble me multiplied so much? Many have risen up against me.

(Psalms 3:3) 
Many say to my very soul, 'There is no salvation for him, not even in his God.'

(Psalms 3:4) 
But You, Oh Lord, You are my protector and defender; You are my glory, and You are the one who lifts up my head.

(Psalms 3:5) 
With my voice, I cried out to the Lord, and He heard me from His holy mountain.

(Psalms 3:6) 
I lay down and fell into a deep sleep; and I awoke again, because the Lord sustains and protects me.

(Psalms 3:7) 
I will not fear the thousands of people surrounding me. Rise up, Oh Lord; save me, Oh my God.

(Psalms 3:8) 
For You have struck down all who opposed me without cause; You have crushed the teeth of sinners, shattering their power and ability to harm.

(Psalms 3:9) 
Salvation belongs to the Lord alone; and Your blessing is upon Your people.

(Psalms 3:10) 
For the End of all things, to be sung with stringed instruments. A Psalm by David.

(Psalms 3:11) 
When I called upon Him, the God of my righteousness heard me. In my tribulation, You made room for me and eased my distress. Have mercy on me, and hear my prayer.

(Psalms 3:12) 
Oh sons of men, how long will your hearts be hardened and heavy with sin? Why do you love vanity and seek after falsehood?

(Psalms 3:13) 
And know this: the Lord has marvelously set apart His holy one. The Lord will hear me when I cry out to Him.

(Psalms 3:14) 
Be angry, but do not sin. What you speak in your hearts, reflect on it in your beds and be pierced with sorrow for it.

(Psalms 3:15) 
Offer the sacrifice of righteousness, and place your hope in the Lord.

(Psalms 3:16) 
Many say, 'Who will show us good things?' The light of Your face, Oh Lord, has been impressed and shone upon us.

(Psalms 3:17) 
You have given joy to my heart, more than the joy they find when their grain, wine, and oil have multiplied and overflowed abundantly.

(Psalms 3:18) 
In peace, I will lie down and rest in that very same hope; for You, Oh Lord, have singularly established me in hope, setting me apart for it.

(Psalms 3:19) 
For the End of all things, concerning the one who obtains the spiritual inheritance. A Psalm by David.

(Psalms 3:20) 
Receive my words into Your ears, Oh Lord; understand the deep meaning of my cry.

(Psalms 3:21) 
Give heed to the voice of my prayer, my King and my God; for I will pray to You alone.

(Psalms 3:22) 
Oh Lord, in the morning You will hear my voice. In the morning, I will stand before You in expectation, and I will see Your answer.

(Psalms 3:23) 
For You are not a God who desires or permits iniquity. Nor will the wicked dwell near You;

(Psalms 3:24) 
nor will the unjust endure or remain before Your eyes.

(Psalms 3:25) 
You hate all who practice iniquity; You will destroy all who speak lies.

(Psalms 3:26) 
The Lord will utterly detest the man who sheds blood and is full of deceit.

(Psalms 3:27) 
But I, in the abundance of Your mercy, will enter into Your house; I will worship toward Your holy temple with reverent fear of You.

(Psalms 3:28) 
Oh Lord, lead me in Your righteousness; because of my enemies, guide my path directly before Your face.

(Psalms 3:29) 
For there is no truth in their mouths; their heart is empty and vain. Their throat is an open sepulchre, a source of corruption; with their tongues, they acted deceitfully. Judge them, Oh God.

(Psalms 3:30) 
Let them fall short of their own schemes; according to the multitude of their impieties, cast them out, for they have provoked You, Oh Lord, to anger.

(Psalms 3:31) 
And let all who hope in You rejoice; they will exult forever, and You will overshadow them with Your protection. And all who love Your name will glory in You.

(Psalms 3:32) 
For You, Oh Lord, will bless the just person. You have crowned us with the shield of Your good will, providing us with ultimate defense and favor.

(Psalms 3:33) 
For the End of all things, to be sung with stringed instruments, on the eighth note. A Psalm by David.

(Psalms 3:34) 
Oh Lord, do not rebuke me in Your burning fury, nor chasten me in Your intense anger.

(Psalms 3:35) 
Have mercy on me, Oh Lord, for I am weak and frail. Heal me, Oh Lord, for my very bones are troubled and shaken.

(Psalms 3:36) 
And my soul is greatly troubled and disturbed; but You, Oh Lord, how long will this last?

(Psalms 3:37) 
Turn back to me, Oh Lord, and rescue my soul; save me because of Your steadfast mercy.

(Psalms 3:38) 
For among the dead, there is no one who remembers You; and in the underworld (Sheol), who will give You praise or confess Your name?

(Psalms 3:39) 
I am exhausted with my groaning; every single night I will wash my bed with tears. With my tears, I will drench and saturate my couch.

(Psalms 3:40) 
My eye is troubled and dimmed by my anguish; I have grown old and weary among all my enemies.

(Psalms 4:1) 
For the End. With stringed instruments. A Psalm of David.

(Psalms 4:2) 
When I called out, the God who is my righteousness heard me. You brought me relief in my distress. Have mercy on me, and hear my prayer.

(Psalms 4:3) 
O sons of men, how long will your hearts be so hardened? Why do you love empty things and seek out lies?

(Psalms 4:4) 
Know this: the Lord has wonderfully set apart His holy one. The Lord will hear me when I cry out to Him.

(Psalms 4:5) 
Be angry, but do not sin. The things you say in your hearts—reflect on them in your beds and be contrite.

(Psalms 4:6) 
Offer sacrifices that are righteous, and place your hope in the Lord.

(Psalms 4:7) 
Many are saying: 'Who will show us good things?' But the light of Your face, O Lord, is imprinted upon us.

(Psalms 4:8) 
You have put joy in my heart—a joy far greater than the wicked's increase in their grain, wine, and oil.

(Psalms 4:9) 
In peace, I will lie down and rest, for You alone, O Lord, have set me securely in hope.

(Psalms 5:1) 
For the End-Times, for those who will receive their eternal inheritance. A Psalm of David.

(Psalms 5:2) 
Listen closely to my words, O Lord; understand my cry for help.

(Psalms 5:3) 
Pay attention to the sound of my prayer, my King and my God, because I will pray to You.

(Psalms 5:4) 
O Lord, in the morning You will hear my voice; in the morning I will stand before You and I will watch expectantly.

(Psalms 5:5) 
For You are not a God who wills wickedness; nor will the malicious dwell with You.

(Psalms 5:6) 
Nor will the unjust remain before Your eyes; You hate all who work iniquity.

(Psalms 5:7) 
You will destroy all who speak lies; a man of bloodshed and deceit the Lord will abhor.

(Psalms 5:8) 
But I, in the abundance of Your mercy, will enter into Your house; I will worship at Your holy temple in reverent awe of You.

(Psalms 5:9) 
O Lord, lead me in Your justice because of my enemies; direct my way in Your sight.

(Psalms 5:10) 
For there is no truth in their mouths; their inner being is emptiness.

(Psalms 5:11) 
Their throat is an open tomb; with their tongues they acted deceitfully. Judge them, O God: let them fall from their own schemes. According to the multitude of their impieties, cast them out, for they have provoked You, O Lord.

(Psalms 5:12) 
And let all who hope in You rejoice; they will exult eternally, and You will overshadow them; and all who love Your Name will glory in You.

(Psalms 6:1)
For the End. With stringed instruments. A Psalm of David.

(Psalms 6:2) 
O Lord, do not rebuke me when you are full of fury, and do not chastise me when you are full of wrath.

(Psalms 6:3) 
Have mercy on me, O Lord, because I am frail. Heal me, O Lord, because my very bones are disturbed and agitated.

(Psalms 6:4) 
My very soul is also greatly troubled. But you, O Lord, how long will this last?

(Psalms 6:5) 
Turn your attention to me, O Lord, and rescue my soul. Save me for the sake of your tender mercy.

(Psalms 6:6) 
For no one in the realm of death can remember you. And in the underworld, who will be able to praise you?

(Psalms 6:7) 
I have exhausted myself with my groaning. Every night I drench my bed with my tears; my very couch I water with my weeping.

(Psalms 6:8) 
My vision is blurred from anguish; I have grown weary and aged amidst all my enemies.

(Psalms 6:9) 
Go away from me, all you who commit evil deeds, because the Lord has truly heard the sound of my weeping.

(Psalms 6:10) 
The Lord has heard my humble plea; the Lord has accepted my prayer.

(Psalms 6:11) 
Let all my enemies be utterly put to shame and be greatly confounded. Let them retreat, turning away in deep shame, and let it happen very swiftly.

(Psalms 6:1)
For the End. With stringed instruments. A Psalm of David.

(Psalms 6:2) 
My Lord, do not rebuke me by means of Your righteous wrath, nor punish me by means of Your intense anger—for Your anger is always just.

(Psalms 6:3) 
Have mercy on me, My Lord, for I am weak and afflicted; heal me, My Lord, for my entire being is deeply distressed, affecting me to my very core.

(Psalms 6:4) 
And my soul is profoundly troubled, truly disturbed; but You, My Lord, how long will you delay granting my petition?

(Psalms 6:5) 
Turn back to me, My Lord, and rescue my very life—my soul; save me purely by reason of Your loving mercy.

(Psalms 6:6) 
For among those who have died, there is no one who can remember You in praise; and in the realm of the dead, who will confess Your greatness and give You glory?

(Psalms 6:7) 
I am utterly exhausted and worn out from my constant groaning; every single night I drench my sleeping place with tears; with my tears, I completely soak my bed.

(Psalms 6:8) 
My eye is dimmed and swollen from the intensity of my grief and sorrow; I have grown weary and aged amidst all my adversaries.

(Psalms 6:9) 
Depart from me, all you who commit wicked deeds, for the Lord has heard the sound of my weeping and has now answered my prayer.

(Psalms 6:10) 
The Lord has heard my urgent and heartfelt plea; the Lord has indeed accepted my prayer.

(Psalms 6:11) 
May all my enemies be put to shame and be profoundly confused and thrown into disarray; may they turn back from their evil intentions and be shamed very swiftly.

(Psalms 7:1) 
A Psalm of David, which he sang to the Lord concerning the malicious words of Cush, the son of Jemini.

(Psalms 7:2) 
O Lord, my God, in You I have placed my trust. Rescue me from all those who pursue me, and deliver me from their grasp.

(Psalms 7:3) 
Otherwise, they may tear my life away like a lion, with no one to rescue me and no one to save me from their attack.

(Psalms 7:4) 
O Lord, my God, if I have committed this offense—if there is any wickedness on my hands—

(Psalms 7:5) 
if I have repaid evil to those who treated me poorly, then let my enemies justly overtake me and leave me desolate.

(Psalms 7:6) 
Let the enemy pursue my life and capture it. Let him trample my life to the ground and lay my honor in the dust.

(Psalms 7:7) 
Arise, O Lord, in Your righteous anger! Lift Yourself up against the outrage of my enemies. Arise, O Lord my God, by the decree of justice that You have commanded.

(Psalms 7:8) 
Then the assembly of all nations will gather around You to witness Your judgment. Because of this, return to Your high throne to judge them.

(Psalms 7:9) 
The Lord is the judge of all peoples. Judge me, O Lord, according to my righteousness, and according to the blamelessness that is found in me.

(Psalms 7:10) 
Let the wickedness of sinners be brought to an end, but You, O God, will guide the righteous. You are the God who searches the innermost thoughts and desires of hearts and minds.

(Psalms 7:11) 
My righteous help comes from the Lord, who saves all those with an upright heart.

(Psalms 7:12) 
God is a righteous Judge; He is strong and patient. Does He become angry and judge every single day? —No, He is patient.

(Psalms 7:13) 
If you do not repent and turn away from your sins, He will brandish His sword against you. He has already strung His bow and prepared it for judgment.

(Psalms 7:14) 
And in His hand, He has prepared the instruments of death; He has made His arrows burning with divine justice.

(Psalms 7:15) 
Behold, the wicked man has conceived injustice; he has become pregnant with mischief and has given birth to iniquity.

(Psalms 7:16) 
The wicked man opened a pit and dug it deep, but he himself has fallen into the very trap he created.

(Psalms 7:17) 
His mischief will return upon his own head, and his violent iniquity will descend upon his own skull.

(Psalms 7:18) 
I will give thanks to the Lord according to His perfect justice, and I will sing praises to the name of the Lord Most High.

(Psalms 8:1) 
This Psalm is for the chief musician, set to 'The Gittith', a psalm of David. O Lord, our Master, how wonderful is Your name across the entire earth! For Your majesty is lifted up beyond all the created skies and even the spiritual heavens.

(Psalms 8:2) 
From the mouths of babes and suckling infants, You have perfected praise to put Your enemies to shame, so that You might silence every enemy and avenger.

(Psalms 8:3) 
When I consider Your heavens—the work of Your fingers—the moon and the stars that You have set in place:

(Psalms 8:4) 
What is humanity, that You are mindful of it? Or the children of men, that You look after them?

(Psalms 8:5) 
You have made humanity a little lower than the angels, and You have crowned them with glory and honor.

(Psalms 8:6) 
And You have given them dominion over the works of Your hands.

(Psalms 8:7) 
You have put all things under their feet: all sheep and oxen, and also the animals of the field.

(Psalms 8:8) 
The birds of the air and the fish of the sea, who travel the pathways of the sea.

(Psalms 8:9) 
O Lord, our Master, how wonderful is Your name across the entire earth!

(Psalms 8:1) 
For the ultimate fulfillment, a song of the winepresses; A Psalm of David.

(Psalms 8:2) 
O Lord, our Lord, how wonderful and awe-inspiring is your name across the entire earth! For your magnificent glory is raised high above all the created skies and the universe.

(Psalms 8:3) 
From the mouths of infants and nursing babies, you have established strength as a perfect praise, designed to silence your enemies and destroy both the malevolent foe and the avenger.

(Psalms 8:4) 
For when I observe your skies, the very work of your divine fingers, and behold the moon and the stars which you have securely founded and established,

(Psalms 8:5) 
What is humanity that you are so mindful of it? Or what is the son of man, that you would lovingly visit him?

(Psalms 8:6) 
You have made him only a little lower than the angels, and you have crowned him with glory and honor.

(Psalms 8:7) 
And you have set him in authority over the works of your hands; you have placed all things in submission under his feet:

(Psalms 8:8) 
All sheep and oxen, and also the wild beasts of the open field;

(Psalms 8:9) 
The birds of the sky, and the fish of the sea, which traverse the watery pathways of the ocean.

(Psalms 8:10) 
O Lord, our Lord, how wonderful and awe-inspiring is your name across the entire earth!

(Psalms 8:11) 
For the ultimate fulfillment, concerning the hidden mysteries of the Son; A Psalm of David.

(Psalms 8:12) 
I will give thanks to you, O Lord, with my whole heart; I will recount all your wondrous and miraculous deeds.

(Psalms 8:13) 
I will rejoice and exult in your presence; I will sing praises to your holy name, O Most High God.

(Psalms 8:14) 
When my enemies are turned back and retreat, they will stumble, become weak, and perish from before your very presence.

(Psalms 8:15) 
For you have undertaken my judgment and pleaded my cause; you are seated upon your throne, you who judge with perfect justice.

(Psalms 8:16) 
You have rebuked the Gentile nations, and the wicked one has utterly perished; their very name you have erased for all eternity and for every generation to come.

(Psalms 8:17) 
The swords of the enemies have failed, brought to an absolute end, and their cities you have utterly destroyed; their memory has perished with a loud, resounding crash of ruin.

(Psalms 8:18) 
But the Lord remains steadfast forever; He has established His throne ready for the final judgment.

(Psalms 8:19) 
And He himself will judge the entire world with perfect equity and fairness; He will judge all peoples with true justice.

(Psalms 8:20) 
And the Lord has become a secure refuge for the poor; a timely helper in moments of urgent need, and a strong support in tribulation.

(Psalms 8:21) 
And let all those who truly know your name place their hope and trust in you, for you have never forsaken those who earnestly seek you, O Lord.

(Psalms 8:22) 
Sing praises to the Lord, who dwells in the holy city of Zion; declare His mighty deeds and purposes among all the Gentile nations.

(Psalms 8:23) 
For He, who seeks justice for their shed blood, has remembered the wronged; He has not forgotten the piteous cry of the poor and afflicted.

(Psalms 8:24) 
Have mercy on me, O Lord; see my humble affliction caused by my enemies, you who lift me up from the very gates of death,

(Psalms 8:25) 
So that I may proclaim all your praises publicly within the gates of the daughter of Zion, Jerusalem.

(Psalms 8:26) 
I will exult in your saving power; the Gentile nations have become stuck fast in the very pit which they themselves dug.

(Psalms 8:27) 
In that very snare which they cunningly hid, their own foot has been caught.

(Psalms 8:28) 
The Lord will be known and recognized by the judgments He executes; the sinner is caught and entrapped by the works of his own hands.

(Psalms 8:29) 
Let all sinners be turned towards the grave and the underworld, all the Gentile nations that forget God and His ways.

(Psalms 8:30) 
For the poor will not be forgotten permanently; the patient expectation and hope of the afflicted will not perish and will not be lost forever.

(Psalms 8:31) 
Arise, O Lord; do not let humanity prevail by its own strength; let the Gentile nations be judged in your just sight.

(Psalms 8:32) 
Appoint, O Lord, a lawgiver or a terror over them, so that the Gentile nations may truly know that they are merely mortal men and not gods.

(Psalms 8:33) 
Why, O Lord, have you withdrawn so far away? Why do you seem to ignore or hide yourself in times of opportune need, especially during tribulation?

(Psalms 8:34) 
While the wicked person proudly exalts himself, the poor and righteous are inflamed with suffering; they are ensnared by the very schemes which the wicked devise.

(Psalms 8:35) 
For the sinner is praised for the desires of his own soul, and the iniquitous one is seemingly blessed and favored.

(Psalms 8:36) 
The sinner has greatly provoked the Lord; in his abundant pride and wrath, he will not seek out God.

(Psalms 8:37) 
God is not in his thoughts or before his eyes; his ways are corrupted and defiled at every moment.

(Psalms 8:38) 
Your divine judgments are far removed from his consideration, and he boasts that he will surely dominate all his enemies.

(Psalms 8:39) 
For he has said in his heart: 'I will not be shaken for generations to come, and no evil will ever befall me.'

(Psalms 8:40) 
His mouth is full of curses, bitterness, and deceit; beneath his tongue lie trouble and the pain of malice.

(Psalms 9:1) 
To the chief musician, regarding the death of the son (or concerning hidden things of the son). A Psalm of David. I will praise you, Lord, with my whole heart; I will recount all your wondrous deeds.

(Psalms 9:2) 
I will rejoice and exult in you; I will sing praises to your Name, O Most High.

(Psalms 9:3) 
When my enemies turn back in retreat, they will weaken and perish from your presence.

(Psalms 9:4) 
For you have executed my judgment and defended my cause; you have sat upon your throne, judging justly and with righteousness.

(Psalms 9:5) 
You have rebuked the nations and destroyed the wicked; you have blotted out their name forever and for all ages.

(Psalms 9:6) 
The swords and threats of the enemy have come to an end; you have destroyed their cities. Their very memory has perished with a loud crash.

(Psalms 9:7) 
And the Lord remains forever; He has prepared His throne for judgment.

(Psalms 9:8) 
And He Himself will judge the whole earth with equity; He will judge the peoples with justice.

(Psalms 9:9) 
And the Lord has become a refuge for the poor, a helper in times of need, in affliction.

(Psalms 9:10) 
And may those who know your Name—who know your character and power—hope in you, for you have not forsaken those who seek you, Lord.

(Psalms 9:11) 
Sing praises to the Lord who dwells in Zion; proclaim His deeds among the nations.

(Psalms 9:12) 
For seeking justice for their blood, He has remembered; He has not forgotten the cry of the oppressed.

(Psalms 9:13) 
Have mercy on me, Lord; see my lowliness from my enemies, You who lift me up from the gates of death—from the power of the grave itself,

(Psalms 9:14) 
So that I may declare all your praises in the gates of the daughter of Zion. I will exult in your salvation.

(Psalms 9:15) 
The nations are trapped in the destruction they made for others; their foot is caught in the very snare they hid.

(Psalms 9:16) 
The Lord is known by the judgments He executes; the sinner is caught by the works of his own hands. A song. (A musical interlude.)

(Psalms 9:17) 
May sinners be turned into the realm of the dead—all nations that forget God.

(Psalms 9:18) 
For the poor will not be forgotten forever; the patience of the oppressed will not perish eternally.

(Psalms 9:19) 
Arise, Lord, let no human be strengthened against You; let the nations be judged in your sight.

(Psalms 9:20) 
Appoint, Lord, a lawgiver over them, so that the nations may know that they are but men. (A musical interlude.)

(Psalms 9:21) 
Why, Lord, have you withdrawn so far away? Why do you hide yourself in times of need, in affliction?

(Psalms 9:22) 
While the wicked person acts proudly, the poor are set ablaze by his actions; they are caught in the very schemes the wicked devise.

(Psalms 9:23) 
For the sinner is praised for the desires of his own soul, and the unrighteous is blessed by others for his evil ways.

(Psalms 9:24) 
The sinner has provoked the Lord; in the arrogance of his anger, he will not seek God.

(Psalms 9:25) 
There is no God in his sight, so he acts as if God doesn't exist; his ways are defiled at all times. Your judgments are far from his mind; he will lord it over all his enemies.

(Psalms 9:26) 
For he has said in his heart: 'I will not be moved from generation to generation; no misfortune will touch me.'

(Psalms 9:27) 
His mouth is full of cursing, and bitterness, and deceit; under his tongue are mischief and iniquity.

(Psalms 9:28) 
He sits in ambush with the rich in hidden places, so that he may kill the innocent. His eyes watch for the poor.

(Psalms 9:29) 
He lies in wait secretly, like a lion in his den; he lies in wait to seize the poor: to seize the poor when he draws him in.

(Psalms 9:30) 
In his snare, he will bring him low; the poor man will fall into it, when the wicked's strength against the poor increases.

(Psalms 9:31) 
For he has said in his heart: 'God has forgotten, He has turned away His face, so that He will not see until the end.'

(Psalms 9:32) 
Arise, Lord God, let your hand be exalted: do not forget the oppressed.

(Psalms 9:33) 
Why has the wicked person provoked God? For he has said in his heart: 'He will not seek vengeance for my actions.'

(Psalms 9:34) 
You see, for you consider trouble and sorrow, that you may deliver them into your hands. To you the poor is left; you are the helper of the orphan.

(Psalms 9:35) 
Break the arm of the sinner and the malicious one: his sin will be sought out, but none will be found for him to commit.

(Psalms 9:36) 
The Lord will reign forever and for all ages; you, nations, will perish from His land.

(Psalms 9:37) 
The Lord has heard the desire of the oppressed; your ear has heard the preparation of their heart as they prayed.

(Psalms 9:38) 
To judge for the orphan and the humble, so that man may no longer presume to exalt himself upon the earth.

(Psalms 9:39) 
To the chief musician. A Psalm of David. In the Lord I take refuge: how can you say to my soul: 'Flee to the mountain like a sparrow?'

(Psalms 9:40) 
For behold, sinners have bent their bow, they have prepared their arrows in their quiver, so that they may shoot the upright in heart in the darkness of the moon—in secret.

(Psalms 9:1)

(Psalms 9:2) 
I will give You praise, O Lord, with all my heart; I will recount all Your wonderful works.

(Psalms 9:4) 
When my enemy turns back, they will stumble and perish from Your presence.

(Psalms 9:5) 
Because You have upheld my right and my cause; You are seated on Your throne, judging all things with perfect justice.

(Psalms 9:7)

(Psalms 9:8)

(Psalms 9:9)

(Psalms 10:1) 
How long, O Lord, have You withdrawn from us, standing far off and looking down upon us during times of need and tribulation?

(Psalms 10:2) 
When the wicked act with pride, the poor are set aflame with suffering. The poor are trapped by the very plans the wicked devise against them.

(Psalms 10:3) 
For the sinner is praised by others because of the desires of his own soul, and the unrighteous person is seen by many as blessed.

(Psalms 10:4) 
The sinner has provoked the Lord; in the greatness of his pride and anger, he does not seek God's presence or judgment.

(Psalms 10:5) 
God is not in his thoughts. His ways are corrupt at all times. Your judgments, O God, are too high for him to see, and he believes he will dominate all his enemies.

(Psalms 10:6) 
For he has said in his heart: 'I will never be shaken from my position, from generation to generation, and no harm will ever come to me.'

(Psalms 10:7) 
His mouth is full of cursing, bitterness, and deceit. Under his tongue are both trouble and iniquity.

(Psalms 10:8) 
He sits in ambush, hidden with other powerful and rich men, to murder the innocent.

(Psalms 10:9) 
His eyes watch the poor. He lies in wait in secret, like a lion in its den. He lies in wait to seize the poor; he seizes the poor by dragging him into his trap.

(Psalms 10:10) 
With his snare, he humiliates the poor. The poor man is bowed down and falls when the wicked man has gained mastery over him.

(Psalms 10:11) 
For he has said in his heart: 'God has forgotten. He has turned away His face so that He will never see anything.'

(Psalms 10:12) 
Arise, O Lord God! Let Your hand be lifted high in power. Do not forget the suffering poor.

(Psalms 10:13) 
Why has the wicked man provoked God? For he has said in his heart: 'God will not seek or investigate these things.'

(Psalms 10:14) 
You see it all, for You consider the trouble and sorrow of the poor, so that You may take them into Your hands. The poor man is left to Your care; You will be the helper for the orphan.

(Psalms 10:15) 
Break the power of the wicked and malicious sinner. His sin will be sought out, but it will not be found; it will be utterly removed.

(Psalms 10:16) 
The Lord will reign forever, throughout all ages. The nations that oppose Him will perish from His land.

(Psalms 10:17) 
The Lord has heard the desire of the poor. Your ear has listened to the preparation of their heart, the intentions of their prayers.

(Psalms 10:18) 
You will judge on behalf of the orphan and the humble, so that man will no longer presume to exalt himself on the earth.

(Psalms 10:1) 
For the Consummation: A Psalm of David. (Commentary: "In finem" signifies the ultimate purpose or fulfillment, often understood eschatologically in Christian tradition, pointing to Christ.)

(Psalms 10:2) 
I take my refuge in the Lord. How can you say to my soul: "Flee to the mountain like a small bird?"

(Psalms 10:3) 
For behold, the wicked have drawn their bows; they have made ready their arrows in their quivers, to shoot under cover of darkness at the upright in heart.

(Psalms 10:4) 
For what You, O Lord, have established, they have torn down. But what can the righteous do in such times?

(Psalms 10:5) 
The Lord is in His holy temple; the Lord's throne is in the heavens above, where He reigns. His eyes look upon the afflicted; His gaze examines the children of men.

(Psalms 10:6) 
The Lord examines the righteous and the wicked. But he who loves wickedness hates his own soul, bringing destruction upon himself.

(Psalms 10:7) 
He will rain down snares upon the wicked. Fire and brimstone, and a tempestuous wind, are the portion of their cup—their decreed fate.

(Psalms 10:8) 
For the Lord is righteous, and He loves acts of righteousness. His countenance beholds uprightness and justice.

(Psalms 10:9) 
For the Consummation. For the Eighth String (a musical instruction): A Psalm of David.

(Psalms 10:10) 
Save me, O Lord, for the holy person has vanished. Truths have diminished among the children of men.

(Psalms 10:11) 
They have spoken falsehoods, each one to his neighbor. They have spoken with deceptive lips and a divided heart, meaning they say one thing and believe another.

(Psalms 10:12) 
The Lord will bring to an end the scattered words and the boastful tongue.

(Psalms 10:13) 
All who speak with deceitful lips and a boastful tongue will be silenced.

(Psalms 10:14) 
He will deal with those who have said: "We will make our tongue great. Our lips are our own power. Who is our master?"

(Psalms 10:15) 
Because of the misery of the needy and the groaning of the poor, "Now I will arise," says the Lord. "I will place him in safety; I will act with certainty for him."

(Psalms 10:16) 
The words of the Lord are pure words. They are like silver tested by fire, purified seven times in the crucible of the earth, meaning they are utterly flawless.

(Psalms 10:17) 
You, O Lord, will preserve us and keep us safe from this evil generation forever.

(Psalms 10:18) 
For the Consummation: A Psalm of David.

(Psalms 10:19) 
How long, O Lord, will You forget me completely? How long will You turn Your face away from me?

(Psalms 10:20) 
How long must I harbor anxieties in my soul, and sorrow in my heart day after day?

(Psalms 10:21) 
How long will my enemy be exalted over me?

(Psalms 10:22) 
Look upon me and hear me, O Lord my God. Enlighten my eyes with Your truth, lest I ever fall asleep in the sleep of death, losing hope and faith.

(Psalms 10:23) 
Let my enemy never say, "I have prevailed against him." Let those who trouble me not rejoice if I am moved from my faith.

(Psalms 10:24) 
For the Consummation: A Psalm of David.

(Psalms 10:25) 
The fool has said in his heart, "There is no God." They have become corrupt and abominable in their pursuits. There is no one who does good, not even one person.

(Psalms 10:26) 
The Lord looked down from the heavens upon the children of men to see if there was anyone who understood, or anyone who sought God.

(Psalms 10:27) 
All have turned away; together they have become useless. There is no one who does good, not even one. Their throat is like an open tomb, their tongues practice deceit. The venom of asps is under their lips. Their mouth is full of cursing and bitterness. Their feet are swift to shed blood. Destruction and misery are in their ways, and they have not known the path of peace. There is no fear of God before their eyes.

(Psalms 10:28) 
Will they not come to know, all those who work wickedness, who devour My people as if they were bread to be eaten?

(Psalms 10:29) 
They have not called upon God. There, they trembled with fear where no fear truly existed.

(Psalms 10:30) 
For the Lord is with the righteous generation. You have confounded the plan of the poor, because the Lord is his protector.

(Psalms 10:31) 
Who will grant salvation to Israel from Sion? When the Lord reverses the captivity of His people, Jacob will rejoice, and Israel will be glad.

(Psalms 10:32) 
A Psalm of David. O Lord, who will dwell in Your tabernacle? Or who will rest on Your holy mountain?

(Psalms 10:33) 
He who walks without blemish, and practices righteousness;

(Psalms 10:34) 
he who speaks truth in his heart, who has not practiced deceit with his tongue, nor done evil to his neighbor, nor taken up a reproach against his neighbors;

(Psalms 10:35) 
the wicked person is brought to nothing in his sight, but he glorifies those who fear the Lord. He who swears to his neighbor and does not deceive him;

(Psalms 10:36) 
he who has not lent his money at interest, and has not accepted bribes against the innocent. He who does these things will not be moved from his righteous state forever.

(Psalms 10:37) 
An inscription of a title belonging to David. Preserve me, O Lord, for in You I have placed my hope and trust.

(Psalms 10:38) 
I said to the Lord: "You are my God, for You have no need of my good deeds or possessions."

(Psalms 10:39) 
For the saints who are on His earth, He has made all my desires wonderful in them, fulfilling His will through them.

(Psalms 10:40) 
The infirmities of those who worship other gods have multiplied; after this, they hastened to their ruin. I will not gather their assemblies of bloody sacrifices, nor will I remember their names with my lips.

(Psalms 11:1) 
This Psalm is for the End Times. A Psalm of David. I place my complete trust in the Lord. How can you say to my very soul: 'You must flee to the mountains, like a bird escaping a trap?'

(Psalms 11:2) 
For, just look at this: the wicked have strung their bows and are aiming. They have their arrows ready in their quivers. Their goal is to shoot, from the cover of darkness, those who are righteous in heart.

(Psalms 11:3) 
Because they have torn down everything good that You, O Lord, have established and perfected. When such things are destroyed, what good can the righteous do?

(Psalms 11:4) 
The Lord resides in His holy temple. The Lord has His throne in the universe. His eyes are observing the humble and the suffering, and His gaze carefully scrutinizes all humanity.

(Psalms 11:5) 
The Lord thoroughly investigates both the righteous and the wicked. But anyone who loves evil hates his own soul, condemning himself.

(Psalms 11:6) 
He will rain down snares upon the wicked: fire, burning sulfur, and the consuming winds of a tempest. This will be the cup of judgment they must drink.

(Psalms 11:7) 
Because the Lord is righteous, and He loves acts of justice and righteousness. His very face beholds and favors all that is equitable and right.

(Psalms 11:1) 
In the Lord I trust. How do you say to my very self: "Flee to the mountains like a sparrow?"

(Psalms 11:2) 
For behold, the wicked have aimed their bows; they have prepared their arrows in their quivers, so that in the darkness they may shoot at those who are upright in heart.

(Psalms 11:3) 
For the moral order you established, they have destroyed. But the righteous man, what has he done in response?

(Psalms 11:4) 
The Lord is in His holy temple; the Lord’s throne is in His celestial dwelling.

(Psalms 11:5) 
His eyes look upon the poor; His eyelids scrutinize the children of men.

(Psalms 11:6) 
The Lord examines both the righteous and the wicked; but His very being detests him who loves injustice.

(Psalms 11:7) 
He will rain down snares, fire, and brimstone upon sinners; and a scorching wind will be the portion of their cup.

(Psalms 11:8) 
For the Lord is righteous and loves acts of righteousness; His very presence beholds integrity.

(Psalms 12:1) 
This Psalm is for the ultimate fulfillment—a Psalm by David.

(Psalms 12:2) 
How long, O Lord? Will you forget me completely, forever? How long will you turn your face away from me?

(Psalms 12:3) 
How long must I bear worries in my soul and carry sorrow in my heart all day long?

(Psalms 12:4) 
How long will my enemy triumph over me?

(Psalms 12:5) 
Look on me and hear me, O Lord my God. Enlighten my eyes, lest I ever sleep the sleep of death:

(Psalms 12:6) 
Lest my enemy ever say, 'I have overcome him.' Those who trouble me will rejoice if I am shaken.

(Psalms 12:7) 
But I have hoped in your mercy. My heart will rejoice in your salvation. I will sing to the Lord, who grants good things to me:

(Psalms 12:8) 
And I will sing praise to the name of the Lord Most High.

(Psalms 12:1) 
A Psalm of David, for the ultimate purpose [of salvation], to be sung to the accompaniment of an eight-stringed instrument.

(Psalms 12:2) 
Save me, Lord, because the holy have grown few. Because true teachings have been diminished among all people.

(Psalms 12:3) 
They have spoken empty words, each one to their neighbor. With flattering lips and a deceitful heart, they spoke.

(Psalms 12:4) 
May the Lord destroy all deceitful lips and every boastful tongue.

(Psalms 12:5) 
Those who say: 'We will make our mouths sound great! Our tongue is ours alone! Who is our master?'

(Psalms 12:6) 
Because of the misery of the needy and the groaning of the poor, now I will arise, says the Lord. I will place them in salvation. I will act confidently in it.

(Psalms 12:7) 
The words of the Lord are pure words, like silver tested by fire, purged of impurities from the earth seven times over.

(Psalms 12:8) 
You, Lord, will preserve us, and You will guard us from this generation forever.

(Psalms 12:9) 
How long, Lord? Will You forget me forever? How long will You turn Your face away from me?

(Psalms 12:10) 
How long must I put thoughts in my soul, and sorrow in my heart day after day?

(Psalms 12:11) 
How long will my enemy be exalted over me?

(Psalms 12:12) 
Look at me, and hear me, Lord my God. Enlighten my eyes, lest I ever fall asleep in death.

(Psalms 12:13) 
Lest my enemy ever say, 'I have prevailed against him.' My tormentors will rejoice if I am moved [from my position].

(Psalms 12:14) 
But I have hoped in Your mercy. My heart will rejoice in Your salvation. I will sing to the Lord who has granted me good things, and I will sing praises to the name of the Lord Most High.

(Psalms 12:15) 
A Psalm of David, for the ultimate purpose [of salvation]. The foolish one has said in his heart: 'There is no God.'

(Psalms 12:16) 
They have become corrupt, and abominable in their pursuits. There is no one who does good, not even one.

(Psalms 12:17) 
The Lord looked down from His dwelling place [the spiritual heaven] upon humanity, to see if there is anyone with understanding, or anyone seeking God.

(Psalms 12:18) 
All have turned aside. Together they have become useless. There is no one who does good, not even one.

(Psalms 12:19) 
Their throat is an open tomb. With their tongues, they acted deceitfully. The poison of asps is under their lips.

(Psalms 12:20) 
Their mouth is full of cursing and bitterness. Their feet are swift to shed blood.

(Psalms 12:21) 
Destruction and unhappiness are in their ways, and they have not known the path of peace. There is no fear of God before their eyes.

(Psalms 12:22) 
Will all those who work iniquity not know? Those who devour My people as if they were eating bread?

(Psalms 12:23) 
They have not called upon God. There they will tremble with fear, where there was no [natural] cause for fear.

(Psalms 12:24) 
For the Lord is with the just generation. You have confounded the counsel of the poor, because the Lord is their protector.

(Psalms 12:25) 
Who will bring salvation for Israel from Zion? When the Lord turns away the captivity of His people, Jacob will exult, and Israel will be glad.

(Psalms 12:26) 
A Psalm of David. Lord, who will live in Your tabernacle? Or who will rest on Your holy mountain?

(Psalms 12:27) 
He who walks without blemish, and works justice;

(Psalms 12:28) 
He who speaks truth in his heart, who has not acted deceitfully with his tongue, nor done evil to his neighbor, nor accepted reproach against his neighbors.

(Psalms 12:29) 
The wicked one is brought to nothing in his sight. But he glorifies those who fear the Lord. He who swears to his neighbor and does not deceive;

(Psalms 12:30) 
He who has not lent his money at usury, and has not accepted bribes against the innocent. He who does these things will not be shaken forever.

(Psalms 12:31) 
A title inscription for David himself. Preserve me, Lord, because I have hoped in You.

(Psalms 12:32) 
I said to the Lord: 'You are my God, because You have no need of my good things [my merits].'

(Psalms 12:33) 
To the saints who are on His land, He has fulfilled all my desires in them [through His grace and their intercession].

(Psalms 12:34) 
Their weaknesses have multiplied; afterwards, they hastened. I will not gather their assemblies of bloodshed, nor will I remember their names with my lips.

(Psalms 12:35) 
The Lord is the portion of my inheritance and of my cup. You are the one who will restore my inheritance to me.

(Psalms 12:36) 
The boundary lines have fallen for me in beautiful places. Indeed, my inheritance is beautiful to me.

(Psalms 12:37) 
I will bless the Lord, who has given me understanding. Moreover, even throughout the night, my innermost being [literally 'kidneys'] has instructed me.

(Psalms 12:38) 
I kept the Lord before my sight always, because He is at my right hand, so that I may not be shaken.

(Psalms 12:39) 
Because of this, my heart is glad, and my tongue rejoices. Moreover, my flesh will rest in hope.

(Psalms 12:40) 
Because You will not abandon my soul in the netherworld [Sheol/Hades], nor will You allow Your holy one to see corruption.

(Psalms 13:1) 
The fool says in his heart, "There is no God." They have become corrupt, and their works are abominable; there is no one who does good, not even one person.

(Psalms 13:2) 
The Lord looked down from the sky upon the children of men to see if there was anyone who understood, or anyone who sought God.

(Psalms 13:3) 
Everyone has turned away; they have all become useless. There is no one who does good, not even one. Their throat is like an open tomb; they have dealt deceitfully with their tongues. The venom of asps is under their lips.

(Psalms 13:4) 
Their mouth is full of cursing and bitterness; their feet are swift to shed blood. Destruction and misery are in their ways, and they have not known the way of peace. There is no fear of God before their eyes.

(Psalms 13:5) 
Do all those who work wickedness not know this—those who devour My people as if they were eating bread?

(Psalms 13:6) 
They have not called upon the Lord. There they trembled with fear where there was no reason to fear, because the Lord is with the generation of the just.

(Psalms 13:7) 
You have confounded the plan of the poor, for the Lord is his hope. Who will bring salvation for Israel out of Zion? When the Lord turns away the captivity of His people, Jacob will rejoice, and Israel will be glad.
