(Psalms 48:14) 
For this is God, our God forever, and for ages of ages: He will rule us forever.

(Psalms 49:1) 
Listen to this, all you people;

(Psalms 49:2) 
listen carefully, all who dwell on earth:

(Psalms 49:3) 
people of all classes, people of all kinds, the wealthy and the poor.

(Psalms 49:4) 
My mouth will declare wisdom;

(Psalms 49:5) 
and the meditation of my heart will be prudence.

(Psalms 49:6) 
I will incline my ear to a parable;

(Psalms 49:7) 
I will open my proposition in the psalter.

(Psalms 49:8) 
Why will I be afraid in the evil day? The iniquity of my heel will surround me.

(Psalms 49:9) 
They trust in their own strength, and glory in the multitude of their riches.

(Psalms 49:10) 
A brother will not redeem, nor will a man redeem, nor give to God his ransom,

(Psalms 49:11) 
nor the price of the redemption of his soul.

(Psalms 49:12) 
And he will labor in eternity, and will live forever.

(Psalms 49:13) 
For he will not see corruption when he sees the wise dying;

(Psalms 49:14) 
at the same time, the foolish and the stupid will perish: and they will leave their riches to others.

(Psalms 49:15) 
And their sepulchers are their homes forever, their tabernacles from generation to generation.

(Psalms 49:16) 
They set their tongues, and they called the lands by their names.

(Psalms 49:17) 
And man, when he was in honor, did not understand.

(Psalms 49:18) 
He is compared to the irrational beasts, and made similar to them.

(Psalms 49:19) 
This is their way: it is a scandal to them: and afterwards they will be pleased in their mouth.

(Psalms 49:20) 
As sheep are placed in hell: death will feed on them. And the just will rule over them in the morning: and their help will be consumed by old age in hell.

(Psalms 49:21) 
But God will redeem my soul from the hand of hell, when he receives me.

(Psalms 49:22) 
Do not fear when he becomes rich, and when the glory of his house is multiplied.

(Psalms 49:23) 
For when he dies, he will take nothing.

(Psalms 49:24) 
And his glory will not descend with him.

(Psalms 49:25) 
Because his soul will be blessed in his life.

(Psalms 49:26) 
He will confess to you when you receive, and you will repay him.

(Psalms 49:27) 
He will enter into the generation of his fathers: he will never see the light.

(Psalms 49:28) 
Man, when he was in honor, did not understand: he is compared to the irrational beasts, and made similar to them.

(Psalms 50:1) 
Have mercy on me, God, according to Your mercy.

(Psalms 50:2) 
And according to the abundance of Your compassion, erase my iniquity.

(Psalms 50:3) 
Wash me thoroughly from my iniquity, and cleanse me from my sin.

(Psalms 50:4) 
For I acknowledge my iniquity, and my sin is always before me.

(Psalms 50:5) 
Against You alone have I sinned, and done what is evil in Your sight, so that You may be justified in Your words, and prevail when You are judged.

(Psalms 50:6) 
For behold, I was conceived in iniquities, and in sins did my mother conceive me.

(Psalms 50:7) 
Behold, You have desired truth; You have made known to me the uncertain and hidden things of Your wisdom.

(Psalms 50:8) 
You will sprinkle me with hyssop, and I shall be cleansed; You will wash me, and I shall be whiter than snow.

(Psalms 50:9) 
You will give me joy and gladness; and the bones that were humbled shall rejoice.

(Psalms 50:10) 
Turn Your face away from my sins, and blot out all my iniquities.

(Psalms 50:11) 
Create a clean heart in me, God, and renew a steadfast spirit within me.

(Psalms 50:12) 
Do not cast me away from Your presence, and do not take Your Holy Spirit from me.

(Psalms 50:13) 
Restore to me the joy of Your salvation, and strengthen me with a willing spirit.

(Psalms 50:14) 
Then I will teach the wicked Your ways, and sinners will be converted to You.

(Psalms 50:15) 
Deliver me from bloodguiltiness, God, God of my salvation, and my tongue will rejoice in Your justice.

(Psalms 50:16) 
O Lord, You will open my lips, and my mouth will declare Your praise.

(Psalms 50:17) 
For if You had desired sacrifice, I would have given it; You will not delight in burnt offerings.

(Psalms 50:18) 
The sacrifice for God is a contrite spirit; a contrite and humbled heart, God, You will not despise.

(Psalms 50:19) 
Be gracious, O Lord, in Your good pleasure to Zion, that the walls of Jerusalem may be rebuilt.

(Psalms 50:20) 
Then You will accept the sacrifice of justice, offerings, and burnt offerings; then they will place young bulls upon Your altar.

(Psalms 51:1) 
Have mercy on me, O God, because of Your great mercy.

(Psalms 51:2) 
And because of Your compassion, wipe away my iniquity.

(Psalms 51:3) 
Wash me completely from my sin and cleanse me.

(Psalms 51:4) 
Because I know my iniquities, my sins are always before me.

(Psalms 51:5) 
I have sinned against You alone, and done what is evil in Your eyes, so that You are just in Your sentence, and righteous in Your judgment.

(Psalms 51:6) 
Behold, I was conceived in iniquity, and in sin did my mother conceive me.

(Psalms 51:7) 
Indeed, You love truth in the heart; You have made known to me the secrets of Your wisdom.

(Psalms 51:8) 
Purge me with hyssop, and I shall be clean; wash me, and I shall be whiter than snow.

(Psalms 51:9) 
Make me hear joy and gladness; that the bones You have crushed may rejoice.

(Psalms 51:10) 
Turn Your face away from my sins, and blot out all my iniquities.

(Psalms 51:11) 
Create in me a clean heart, O God, and renew a right spirit within me.

(Psalms 51:12) 
Do not cast me away from Your presence, and do not take Your Holy Spirit from me.

(Psalms 51:13) 
Restore to me the joy of Your salvation, and sustain me with a willing spirit.

(Psalms 51:14) 
Then I will teach transgressors Your ways, and sinners will return to You.

(Psalms 51:15) 
Deliver me from bloodguiltiness, O God, God of my salvation, and my tongue will sing of Your righteousness.

(Psalms 51:16) 
O Lord, open my lips, and my mouth will proclaim Your praise.

(Psalms 51:17) 
For You do not delight in sacrifice; You would accept a burnt offering.

(Psalms 51:18) 
My sacrifice, O God, is a broken spirit; a broken and contrite heart, O God, You will not despise.

(Psalms 51:19) 
Be pleased to do good to Zion in Your good pleasure; rebuild the walls of Jerusalem.

(Psalms 51:20) 
Then You will be pleased with sacrifices of righteousness, with burnt offerings and whole burnt offerings; then they will offer bulls on Your altar.

(Psalms 52:1) 
For the director of music. A Psalm of David, reflecting deep sorrow.

(Psalms 52:2) 
The fool has said in his heart, “There is no God.”

(Psalms 52:3) 
They are corrupt. They have done detestable deeds, none of them does good.

(Psalms 52:4) 
God looks down from the sky on humankind, to see if there are any who understand, who seek after God.

(Psalms 52:5) 
Everyone has turned away, together they have become useless; no one does good, not even one.

(Psalms 52:6) 
Do all those evildoers not know? They devour my people as though they were bread.

(Psalms 52:7) 
They do not call on God.

(Psalms 52:8) 
They were in great fear, though there was no reason to fear, because God scattered the bones of those who pleased humanity. They were shamed, because God rejected them.

(Psalms 52:9) 
Who will bring salvation for Israel from Zion? When God restores the fortunes of His people, Jacob will rejoice and Israel will be glad.

(Psalms 53:1) 
To the end. A Psalm of David.

(Psalms 53:2) 
The fool has said in his heart, "There is no God."

(Psalms 53:3) 
They have become corrupt; they have become abominable in their wickedness. There is no one who does good.

(Psalms 53:4) 
God looked down from the sky upon the sons of men, to see if there were any who understood, or sought God.

(Psalms 53:5) 
All have turned aside; they have together become useless. There is none who does good, not even one.

(Psalms 53:6) 
Will they not know, all who work iniquity, who devour my people as if they were bread?

(Psalms 53:7) 
They have not called upon God.

(Psalms 53:8) 
There they trembled with fear where there was no fear.

(Psalms 53:9) 
For God has scattered the bones of those who please men; they are confused, because God has despised them.

(Psalms 53:10) 
Who will give from Zion the salvation of Israel? When God returns the captivity of his people, Jacob will rejoice, and Israel will be glad.

(Psalms 54:1) 
For the leader. A song of contemplation by David.

(Psalms 54:2)

(Psalms 54:3)

(Psalms 54:4) 
by the voice of the enemy, and by the oppression of the sinner.

(Psalms 54:5) 
For they have poured wickedness upon me, and they were angry with me.

(Psalms 54:6) 
My heart is troubled within me, and the fear of death has fallen upon me.

(Psalms 54:7) 
Fear and trembling have come upon me, and darkness has covered me.

(Psalms 54:8) 
And I said: “Who will give me wings like a dove, so I can fly away, and be at rest?”

(Psalms 54:9) 
Behold, I have fled far away and remained in the wilderness.

(Psalms 54:10) 
I was waiting for Him to save me from the spirit of the storm and the tempest.

(Psalms 54:11) 
Hasten, Lord; divide their tongues; for I have seen wickedness and contradiction in the city.

(Psalms 54:12) 
Day and night, wickedness surrounds it on its walls, and trouble is in its midst.

(Psalms 54:13) 
Wickedness is in the midst of it, and deceit and fraud never depart from its streets.

(Psalms 54:14) 
For it was not an enemy who reproached me, and I would have borne it. If he who hated me had spoken great things against me, I would perhaps have hidden myself.

(Psalms 54:15) 
But it was you, a man of one mind with me, my guide and my acquaintance.

(Psalms 54:16) 
Together, we took pleasure in food. We walked in the house of God with agreement.

(Psalms 54:17) 
Let death come upon them, and let them go down to hell alive, for wickedness is in their dwellings, in their midst.

(Psalms 54:18) 
But I cried out to God, and the Lord will save me.

(Psalms 54:19) 
In the evening, in the morning, and at noon, I will tell and announce it. And He will hear my voice.

(Psalms 54:20) 
He will redeem my soul in peace from those who call me. For they were with me, though they are many.

(Psalms 54:21) 
May God hear and humble them—He who is before the ages. For there is no change in them, and they did not fear God.

(Psalms 54:22) 
He stretched out his hand to repay. They have defiled His covenant.

(Psalms 54:23) 
They were separated from the wrath of His countenance, and their hearts drew near.

(Psalms 54:24) 
His words are softer than oil, but they are weapons.

(Psalms 54:25) 
Cast your care upon the Lord, and He will nourish you. He will not give the just to be in a perpetual state of fluctuation.

(Psalms 54:26) 
But you, God, will lead them into the pit of destruction. Men of blood and deceit will not live out half their days. But I will trust in you, Lord.

(Psalms 68:15)

(Psalms 68:16) 
The mountain of God is a rich mountain: a congealed mountain, a rich mountain.

(Psalms 68:17) 
Why do you suspect the congealed mountains? The mountain in which it pleased God to dwell: for the Lord will dwell to the end.

(Psalms 68:18) 
The chariots of God are manifold, of ten thousand, of thousands rejoicing: the Lord is among them in Sinai, in the holy place.

(Psalms 68:19) 
You ascended on high, You led captivity captive, You received gifts among men: for even those who do not believe, may dwell, that the Lord God may dwell.

(Psalms 68:20) 
Blessed be the Lord day by day: may God, the God of our salvation, give us a prosperous journey.

(Psalms 68:21) 
Our God is the God of saving: and of the Lord, the Lord is the way out of death.

(Psalms 68:22) 
But indeed God will break the heads of His enemies: the hair of the head of those walking in their wickedness.

(Psalms 68:23) 
The Lord said: "I will bring back from Basan, I will bring back from the depths of the sea:

(Psalms 68:24) 
That your foot may be dipped in blood: the tongue of your dogs from the enemies.

(Psalms 68:25) 
Your footsteps have been seen, O God: the footsteps of my God, my King, Who is in the holy place.

(Psalms 68:26) 
The princes came together before those who were singing psalms: in the midst of the young women playing timbrels.

(Psalms 68:27) 
In the churches, bless God the Lord from the fountains of Israel.

(Psalms 68:28) 
There is little Benjamin in the beginnings, in a state of ecstasy. The princes of Judah, their leaders: the princes of Zabulon, the princes of Naphtali.

(Psalms 68:29) 
Command, O God, Your strength: confirm this, O God, that You have worked in us.

(Psalms 68:30) 
From Your temple in Jerusalem, kings will offer gifts to You.

(Psalms 68:31) 
Rebuke the wild beasts of the reed: the congregation of bulls among the cows of the peoples, so that they may exclude those who are tried by silver: scatter the nations who desire war.

(Psalms 68:32) 
Envoys will come from Egypt: Ethiopia will stretch out its hands to God.

(Psalms 68:33) 
O kingdoms of the earth, sing to God: sing a psalm to the Lord.

(Psalms 68:34) 
Sing to God, Who ascends above the skies of the heavens in the east: behold, He will give to His voice, the voice of strength.

(Psalms 68:35) 
Ascribe glory to God: His magnificence is above Israel, and His power is in the clouds.

(Psalms 68:36) 
God is wonderful in His holy ones: God of Israel Himself will give strength and fortitude to His people. Blessed be God.

(Psalms 70:1) 
In You, Lord, I have placed my hope. May I never be humiliated.

(Psalms 70:2) 
Free me with Your justice, and rescue me. Hear my prayer, and save me.

(Psalms 70:3) 
Be to me a God who protects, and a strong place where you can save me:

(Psalms 70:4) 
For You are my strength, and my refuge. And because of Your name, lead me to safety, and nourish me.

(Psalms 70:5) 
Bring me out of the trap they set for me. Because You are my protector.

(Psalms 70:6) 
Into Your hands I commend my spirit: You have redeemed me, Lord, God of truth.

(Psalms 70:7) 
You hate those who observe false idols. But I have placed my hope in the Lord.

(Psalms 70:8) 
I will rejoice and exult in Your mercy. Because You have seen my lowliness, and saved my soul from its troubles.

(Psalms 70:9) 
You have not handed me over to my enemy. You have set my feet in a spacious place.

(Psalms 70:10) 
Have mercy on me, Lord, because I am in trouble. My eye is troubled in anger, my soul, and my belly.

(Psalms 70:11) 
For my life has failed in sorrow, and my years in groaning. My strength has become weak in poverty, and my bones have been disturbed.

(Psalms 70:12) 
I have become a reproach to all my enemies, and greatly to my neighbors. And a fear to my acquaintances.

(Psalms 70:13) 
Those who saw me, fled far away from me.

(Psalms 70:14) 
I am forgotten, as if I were dead from the heart. I have become like a broken vessel.

(Psalms 70:15) 
For I have heard the reproach of many who live around me. While they gather together against me, they plan to take my life.

(Psalms 70:16) 
But I have hoped in You, Lord. I said: “You are my God: In Your hands are my lots.”

(Psalms 70:17) 
Rescue me from the hand of my enemies, and from those who persecute me.

(Psalms 70:18) 
Shine Your face upon Your servant. Save me in Your mercy.

(Psalms 70:19) 
Lord, may I not be humiliated, because I have called upon You. May the wicked be humiliated, and led down to hell.

(Psalms 70:20) 
May deceitful mouths speak wickedness against the just man, in contempt and in persecuting him.

(Psalms 70:21) 
How great is the multitude of Your sweetness, Lord, which You have hidden for those who fear You. You have prepared it for those who hope in You, in the sight of the sons of men.

(Psalms 70:22) 
You will hide them in the secret of Your face, from the turmoil of men. You will protect them in Your tabernacle from the contradiction of tongues.

(Psalms 70:23) 
Blessed is the Lord, because He has shown His mercy wonderfully to me in a city of defense.

(Psalms 70:24) 
But I said in the excess of my mind: “I am cast out from the face of Your eyes.” Therefore You have heard the voice of my prayer while I cried to You.

(Psalms 70:25) 
Love the Lord, all you His saints. Because the Lord will seek the truth, and will reward those who act with pride abundantly.

(Psalms 70:26) 
Act with courage, and let your heart be strengthened, all you who hope in the Lord.

(Psalms 71:4)

(Psalms 71:5)

(Psalms 71:16)

(Psalms 71:17)

(Psalms 71:18) 
Show your face to your servant: save me in your mercy.

Blessed be the Lord, for he has wonderfully shown his mercy to me in a fortified city.

(Psalms 71:25)

(Psalms 72:1) 
God, grant your judgment to the king, and your justice to the king's son.

(Psalms 72:2) 
May he judge your people justly, and the poor with righteousness.

(Psalms 72:3) 
May the mountains bring peace to the people, and the hills, justice.

(Psalms 72:4) 
May he judge the poor of the people, and save the children of the poor, and humiliate the oppressor.

(Psalms 72:5) 
May he endure as long as the sun and moon, from generation to generation.

(Psalms 72:6) 
May he come down like rain on the fleece, and like the drops falling on the earth.

(Psalms 72:7) 
In his days, justice will flourish, and an abundance of peace, until the moon is no more.

(Psalms 72:8) 
May he have dominion from sea to sea, and from the river to the ends of the earth.

(Psalms 72:9) 
Before him, the Ethiopians will fall prostrate; and his enemies will lick the dust.

(Psalms 72:10) 
The kings of Tarshish and the islands will offer gifts; the kings of Arabia and Saba will bring offerings.

(Psalms 72:11) 
And all the kings of the earth will adore him; all nations will serve him.

(Psalms 72:12) 
For he will free the poor from the oppressor and the poor who have no helper.

(Psalms 72:13) 
He will spare the poor and the needy, and will save the souls of the poor.

(Psalms 72:14) 
From usury and injustice he will redeem their souls, and their name will be honorable before him.

(Psalms 72:15) 
And he will live, and he will be given gold from Arabia. They will adore him always; they will bless him all day long.

(Psalms 72:16) 
May there be a foundation in the land, on the tops of the mountains; may his fruit be exalted above Lebanon, and may they flourish from the city like the grass of the earth.

(Psalms 72:17) 
May his name be blessed forever. May his name endure before the sun.

(Psalms 72:18) 
And in him, all the tribes of the earth will be blessed. All nations will magnify him.

(Psalms 72:19) 
Blessed be the Lord God of Israel, who alone does marvelous things.

(Psalms 72:20) 
And blessed be the name of his majesty forever. May his majesty fill the whole earth. Amen, so be it.

(Psalms 72:21) 
The work of David, the son of Jesse, is finished.

(Psalms 73:1) 
How good is the God of Israel to those who are pure of heart!

(Psalms 73:2) 
But my feet had almost stumbled. My steps were nearly unsteady.

(Psalms 73:3) 
Because I envied those who do evil, seeing the peace of sinners.

(Psalms 73:4) 
They have no regard for death, and they live free from all harm.

(Psalms 73:5) 
They have no struggles, and they aren’t struck down with others.

(Psalms 73:6) 
Therefore, pride grips them. They conceal their sin and their wickedness.

(Psalms 73:7) 
Their iniquity has burst forth, like a fat man. They pass into their own wicked desires.

(Psalms 73:8) 
They think of and speak of wickedness, they speak evil things from high places.

(Psalms 73:9) 
They set their mouths in the sky, and their tongues roam the earth.

(Psalms 73:10) 
Therefore, my people turn here, and full days will be found for them.

(Psalms 73:11) 
And they said, “How does God know? Does the Most High have knowledge?”

(Psalms 73:12) 
Behold, these are the sinners. They are rich in this world, and they have obtained riches.

(Psalms 73:13) 
And I said, “Then in vain have I cleansed my heart, and washed my hands in innocence.

(Psalms 73:14) 
I have been struck down all day long, and my chastisement comes every morning.”

(Psalms 73:15) 
If I had said, “I will speak like them,” then I would have rejected the generation of Your children.

(Psalms 73:16) 
And I considered how I could know this; it is a labor in my eyes,

(Psalms 73:17) 
until I enter the sanctuary of God, and then I will understand their end.

(Psalms 73:18) 
But truly You have set them in slippery places. You cast them down while they were lifted up.

(Psalms 73:19) 
How they have become desolate! Suddenly they have failed; they have perished through their own iniquity.

(Psalms 73:20) 
As a dream when one awakens, so, Lord, when You arise, You will despise their image.

(Psalms 73:21) 
Because my heart was inflamed, and my reins were changed;

(Psalms 73:22) 
and I was brought to nothing, and I did not know.

(Psalms 73:23) 
I was like a beast before You, but I am always with You.

(Psalms 73:24) 
I held Your hand, and in Your will You have led me, and You have received me in glory.

(Psalms 73:25) 
For what do I have in the universe? And what do I desire on the earth besides You?

(Psalms 73:26) 
My flesh and my heart failed; God is the God of my heart, and my portion is God forever.

(Psalms 73:27) 
For behold, those who distance themselves from You will perish; You have destroyed everyone who is unfaithful to You.

(Psalms 73:28) 
But for me, to cling to God is good; to put my hope in the Lord God,

(Psalms 73:29) 
that I may proclaim all Your praises in the gates of the daughter of Zion.

(Psalms 74:1) 
For the leader, in understanding. A psalm of David.

(Psalms 74:2) 
Why have you rejected us, God, forever? Is your anger ignited against the sheep of your pasture?

(Psalms 74:3) 
Remember your community, which you have held since the beginning.

(Psalms 74:4) 
Remember the tribe of your inheritance; the holy mountain of Zion, where you dwell.

(Psalms 74:5) 
Lift up your hands against the arrogant of the world. See how the enemy has made a mess of the holy place!

(Psalms 74:6) 
Your enemies brag in the place of your solemn festival.

(Psalms 74:7) 
They put their wickedness to an end; they did not understand.

(Psalms 74:8) 
They ruined your holy places.

(Psalms 74:9) 
They made it dark, and they cannot see what they do.

(Psalms 74:10) 
Indeed, God is our King forever; he has provided salvation here on Earth.

(Psalms 74:11) 
You, by your power, created the sea; you crushed the heads of the great sea monsters in the water.

(Psalms 74:12) 
You smashed the sea monster’s heads; you gave them as food to the Ethiopians.

(Psalms 74:13) 
You broke open the fountains and the torrents; you dried up the river Ethan.

(Psalms 74:14) 
The day is yours, and the night is yours; you created the dawn and the sun.

(Psalms 74:15) 
You made all the boundaries of the earth; you made the summer and the spring.

(Psalms 74:16) 
Remember this, Lord, the enemy has insulted you; and the foolish people have provoked your name.

(Psalms 74:17) 
Do not give the souls of those who praise you to wild beasts; do not forget the souls of your poor people forever.

(Psalms 74:18) 
Take note of your covenant, because those who have been cast down into the darkness of the land are filled with wickedness.

(Psalms 74:19) 
Do not let the humble be humiliated; the poor and needy will praise your name.

(Psalms 74:20) 
Rise up, God, and defend your cause; remember the insults you suffer, which the foolish hurl at you all day long.

(Psalms 74:21) 
Do not forget the voices of your enemies; the pride of those who hate you always rises up.

(Psalms 75:1) 
To the end. A song. A psalm of Asaph.

(Psalms 75:2) 
God is known in Judea, His name is great in Israel.

(Psalms 75:3) 
Peaceful is His dwelling, His home is in Zion.

(Psalms 75:4) 
There, He broke the strength of the bows: He shattered shields, swords, and war.

(Psalms 75:5) 
You are light, shining from the everlasting mountains.

(Psalms 75:6) 
All the foolish in heart were disturbed; they fell into their sleep.

(Psalms 75:7) 
All the rich men found nothing in their hands.

(Psalms 75:8) 
At Your rebuke, O God of Jacob, those who rode horses were made to sleep.

(Psalms 75:9) 
You are to be feared, and who can resist You? From then on, Your wrath reigns.

(Psalms 75:10) 
You made judgment heard from the sky: the land trembled and was still.

(Psalms 75:11) 
When God arose to judge, to save all the meek of the earth.

(Psalms 75:12) 
For the thought of man shall praise You, and the remnants of thought will keep festival for You.

(Psalms 75:13) 
Vow and give to the Lord your God; all who bring gifts around Him.

(Psalms 75:14) 
To Him who is to be feared, to Him who takes away the spirit of princes, to Him who is feared by the kings of the earth.

(Psalms 76:1) 
To the end, for the songs. A psalm of Asaph.

(Psalms 76:2) 
God is known in Judea, and His name is great in Israel.

(Psalms 76:3) 
He has chosen a place of peace, and His home is in Zion.

(Psalms 76:4) 
There, He broke the strength of bows and destroyed shields, swords, and war.

(Psalms 76:5) 
You are glorious and shine brighter than everything. The mountains are filled with prey.

(Psalms 76:6) 
The foolish are troubled in heart and will sleep the sleep of death.

(Psalms 76:7) 
All the wealthy will find nothing in their hands.

(Psalms 76:8) 
At your rebuke, God of Jacob, those who rode horses fell into a deep sleep.

(Psalms 76:9) 
You are terrible, and who can withstand You once your wrath is roused?

(Psalms 76:10) 
From the sky, You made Your judgment known. The earth trembled and was still,

(Psalms 76:11) 
when God rose up to judge, to save all the meek of the earth.

(Psalms 76:12) 
Truly, the thought of man will give thanks to You, and the remainder of thought will keep festival for You.

(Psalms 76:13) 
Make vows and give to the Lord your God, all you who bring gifts around Him.

(Psalms 76:14) 
To the terrible one, who takes away the spirit of princes, who is terrible to the kings of the earth.

(Psalms 77:1) 
Listen to me, my people, and pay attention to my law.

(Psalms 77:2) 
I will speak to you in a parable; I will tell you the mysteries of the past.

(Psalms 77:3) 
What we have heard and known, our fathers have told us.

(Psalms 77:4) 
We will not hide it from our children, from their generation to the next.

(Psalms 77:5) 
We will tell of the Lord's praises and virtues, and His wondrous works.

(Psalms 77:6) 
He established a covenant with Jacob, and the law was made for Israel.

(Psalms 77:7) 
He commanded our fathers to teach them to their children, so that the next generation might know.

(Psalms 77:8) 
The children who would be born and grow up, so they can tell their children.

(Psalms 77:9) 
They must put their hope in God, never forgetting the works of God, and keeping His commandments.

(Psalms 77:10) 
They will not become like their fathers, a perverse and rebellious generation.

(Psalms 77:11) 
A generation that did not keep their hearts right with God, and their spirit did not believe in Him.

(Psalms 77:12) 
The sons of Ephraim, skilled with the bow, turned back in the day of battle.

(Psalms 77:13) 
They did not keep the covenant of God, and they refused to walk in His law.

(Psalms 77:14) 
They forgot His benefits, and the wonders He showed them.

(Psalms 77:15) 
He performed miracles before their fathers in the land of Egypt, in the plain of Zoan.

(Psalms 77:16) 
He split the sea and led them through, and made the waters stand like a wall.

(Psalms 77:17) 
He led them with a cloud by day and with the light of fire all night.

(Psalms 77:18) 
He split the rocks in the desert and gave them drink as from a great depth.

(Psalms 77:19) 
He brought water out of the rock and made the waters run down like rivers.

(Psalms 77:20) 
Yet they continued to sin against Him, provoking the Most High in the desert.

(Psalms 77:21) 
They tested God in their hearts by asking for food to satisfy their craving.

(Psalms 77:22) 
They spoke against God, and said: "Can God prepare a table in the desert?"

(Psalms 77:23) 
Behold, He struck the rock, and waters flowed out, and streams overflowed. Can He also give bread, or prepare a table for His people?

(Psalms 77:24) 
Therefore the Lord heard them and was angry, and fire was kindled against Jacob, and anger went up against Israel.

(Psalms 77:25) 
Because they did not believe in God, nor did they trust in His salvation.

(Psalms 77:26) 
He commanded the clouds above and opened the doors of the heavens.

(Psalms 77:27) 
He rained down manna for them to eat and gave them the bread of heaven.

(Psalms 77:28) 
Man ate the bread of the angels; He sent them food in abundance.

(Psalms 77:29) 
He brought the south wind from the heavens and by His power brought in the south wind.

(Psalms 77:30) 
He rained meat on them like dust and winged birds like the sand of the sea.

(Psalms 77:31) 
He let them fall in the midst of their camp, around their dwellings.

(Psalms 77:32) 
So they ate and were well filled, and He gave them what they craved.

(Psalms 77:33) 
They were not disappointed in their desire; while their food was still in their mouths.

(Psalms 77:34) 
The anger of God arose against them, and He killed the fattest of them and struck down the chosen men of Israel.

(Psalms 77:35) 
In all these things they still sinned and did not believe in His wonders.

(Psalms 77:36) 
So their days were spent in futility, and their years in haste.

(Psalms 77:37) 
When He killed them, they sought Him, and returned and sought God.

(Psalms 77:38) 
They remembered that God was their rock and that the Most High God was their Redeemer.

(Psalms 77:39) 
But they flattered Him with their mouths, and their tongues lied to Him.

(Psalms 77:40) 
For their heart was not steadfast toward Him, nor were they faithful to His covenant.

(Psalms 77:41) 
But He, being merciful, forgave their iniquity and did not destroy them.

(Psalms 77:42) 
He often restrained His anger and did not stir up all His wrath.

(Psalms 77:43) 
He remembered that they were flesh, a wind that passes and does not return.

(Psalms 77:44) 
How often they provoked Him in the desert, and grieved Him in the wasteland?

(Psalms 77:45) 
They turned back and tested God, and vexed the Holy One of Israel.

(Psalms 77:46) 
They did not remember His hand or the day when He redeemed them from the hand of the enemy.

(Psalms 77:47) 
How He performed His signs in Egypt and His wonders in the plain of Zoan.

(Psalms 77:48) 
He turned their rivers to blood, so that they could not drink their streams.

(Psalms 77:49) 
He sent among them swarms of flies that devoured them, and frogs that destroyed them.

(Psalms 77:50) 
He gave their crops to the caterpillar and their labor to the locust.

(Psalms 77:51) 
He destroyed their vines with hail, and their sycamore trees with frost.

(Psalms 77:52) 
He gave over their livestock to the hail and their possessions to the fire.

(Psalms 77:53) 
He sent against them the heat of His anger, wrath, indignation, and trouble, by sending evil angels.

(Psalms 77:54) 
He made a path for His anger; He did not spare their soul from death, but gave their lives over to the plague.

(Psalms 77:55) 
He struck all the firstborn in Egypt, the first issue of their strength in the tents of Ham.

(Psalms 77:56) 
Then He led forth His people like sheep and guided them in the wilderness like a flock.

(Psalms 77:57) 
He led them safely, so that they were not afraid, but the sea overwhelmed their enemies.

(Psalms 77:58) 
He brought them to the border of His holy land, to the mountain which His right hand had won.

(Psalms 77:59) 
He drove out the nations before them; He divided the land to them as an inheritance by lot.

(Psalms 77:60) 
He made the tribes of Israel dwell in their tents.

(Psalms 77:61) 
Then the Lord awoke as one from sleep, like a warrior refreshed with wine.

(Psalms 77:62) 
He struck His enemies in the back; He put them to everlasting shame.

(Psalms 77:63) 
He rejected the tent of Joseph and did not choose the tribe of Ephraim,

(Psalms 77:64) 
But He chose the tribe of Judah, Mount Zion, which He loved.

(Psalms 77:65) 
He built His sanctuary like the high heavens, like the earth that He has established forever.

(Psalms 77:66) 
He chose David His servant and took him from the sheepfolds.

(Psalms 77:67) 
From following the ewes with young, He brought him to shepherd Jacob His people and Israel His inheritance.

(Psalms 77:68) 
So he shepherded them with a blameless heart and guided them by his skillful hand.

(Psalms 78:1) 
Pay attention, my people, and listen to my law. Open your ears to the words I speak.

(Psalms 78:2) 
I will use parables when I speak; I will speak old stories.

(Psalms 78:3) 
I will tell you all that we have heard, and have learned from our fathers.

(Psalms 78:4) 
We won’t hide these truths from our children, but we will tell them to the next generation.

(Psalms 78:5) 
We will tell how the Lord is worthy of praise, of His mighty deeds and the miracles that He did.

(Psalms 78:6) 
He established a covenant with Jacob and gave His law to Israel. He commanded our ancestors to teach these things to their children,

(Psalms 78:7) 
so that the next generation would know them— the children yet to be born. They would tell their own children.

(Psalms 78:8) 
Then they would put their hope in God, never forget the works of God, and always keep His commandments.

(Psalms 78:9) 
They would not be like their ancestors, a rebellious and stubborn generation, a generation whose heart was not steadfast, and whose spirit was not faithful to God.

(Psalms 78:10) 
The men of Ephraim, though armed with bows and arrows, turned their backs in battle.

(Psalms 78:11) 
They did not keep God’s covenant, and they refused to obey His law.

(Psalms 78:12) 
They forgot His deeds and the miracles that He had shown them.

(Psalms 78:13) 
He performed miracles in front of their fathers, in the land of Egypt, in the plain of Zoan.

(Psalms 78:14) 
He divided the sea and led them through, and He made the waters stand like walls.

(Psalms 78:15) 
He led them with a cloud by day, and with the light of fire all night.

(Psalms 78:16) 
He split rocks in the desert and gave them water as from the depths of the sea.

(Psalms 78:17) 
He caused water to flow from the rock, and made waters run down like rivers.

(Psalms 78:18) 
But they continued to sin against Him; they provoked the Most High in the desert.

(Psalms 78:19) 
They tested God in their hearts, asking for food to satisfy their desires.

(Psalms 78:20) 
They spoke against God, saying, “Can God really prepare a table in the desert?

(Psalms 78:21) 
When he struck the rock, water gushed out, and streams overflowed, but can He also give us bread, or supply meat for His people?”

(Psalms 78:22) 
When the Lord heard them, He was angry. Fire blazed up against Jacob, and wrath rose against Israel,

(Psalms 78:23) 
because they did not believe in God, and did not trust in His salvation.

(Psalms 78:24) 
Yet He commanded the clouds above, and opened the doors of the sky.

(Psalms 78:25) 
He rained down manna for them to eat, giving them the bread of the heavens.

(Psalms 78:26) 
Humans ate the food of angels; He sent them food in abundance.

(Psalms 78:27) 
He sent an east wind from the sky, and by His power brought in the south wind.

(Psalms 78:28) 
He rained down meat on them like dust, and winged birds like the sand of the sea.

(Psalms 78:29) 
He made the birds fall in the middle of their camp, all around their tents.

(Psalms 78:30) 
They ate and were fully satisfied; He gave them what they craved.

(Psalms 78:31) 
But before they could stop eating, and before their cravings were satisfied,

(Psalms 78:32) 
God’s anger rose against them. He killed the strongest among them, and struck down the finest men of Israel.

(Psalms 78:33) 
In spite of all this, they kept sinning; they did not believe in His wonders.

(Psalms 78:34) 
So He brought their days to an end like a breath, and their years in terror.

(Psalms 78:35) 
When He killed them, they sought Him; they repented and earnestly sought God.

(Psalms 78:36) 
Then they remembered that God was their rock, that God Most High was their redeemer.

(Psalms 78:37) 
But they only flattered Him with their mouths; they lied to Him with their tongues.

(Psalms 78:38) 
Their hearts were not sincere toward Him; they were not faithful to His covenant.

(Psalms 78:39) 
But He, being compassionate, forgave their sin and did not destroy them; He often held back His anger, and did not stir up all His wrath.

(Psalms 78:40) 
He remembered that they were but flesh, a wind that passes and does not return.

(Psalms 78:41) 
How often they defied Him in the desert, how often they grieved Him in the wilderness!

(Psalms 78:42) 
Again and again they tested God, and provoked the Holy One of Israel.

(Psalms 78:43) 
They did not remember His power, nor the day when He redeemed them from the oppressor.

(Psalms 78:44) 
He displayed His signs in Egypt, and His wonders in the plain of Zoan.

(Psalms 78:45) 
He turned their rivers to blood, so that they could not drink from their streams.

(Psalms 78:46) 
He sent swarms of flies that devoured them, and frogs that destroyed them.

(Psalms 78:47) 
He gave their crops to the locusts, and the fruit of their labor to the grasshoppers.

(Psalms 78:48) 
He destroyed their vines with hail, and their sycamore-fig trees with frost.

(Psalms 78:49) 
He gave over their cattle to the hail, and their flocks to the lightning.

(Psalms 78:50) 
He unleashed against them the heat of His anger, His wrath, indignation, and trouble—a band of destroying angels.

(Psalms 78:51) 
He made a path for His anger; He did not spare their lives from death, but gave their lives over to the plague.

(Psalms 78:52) 
He struck down all the firstborn in Egypt, the firstfruits of their strength in the tents of Ham.

(Psalms 78:53) 
But He led out His people like a flock; He guided them like a flock through the desert.

(Psalms 78:54) 
He led them safely, and they were not afraid, while the sea engulfed their enemies.

(Psalms 78:55) 
He brought them to the border of His holy land, to the mountain His right hand had won.

(Psalms 78:56) 
He drove out the nations before them, and apportioned their land as an inheritance by lot.

(Psalms 78:57) 
He made the tribes of Israel dwell in their tents.

(Psalms 78:58) 
But they tested and defied God Most High, and did not keep His decrees.

(Psalms 78:59) 
Like their ancestors, they turned back and were faithless; they were like a treacherous bow.

(Psalms 78:60) 
The men of Ephraim, armed with bows, turned back in the day of battle.

(Psalms 78:61) 
They did not keep God’s covenant and refused to live by His law.

(Psalms 78:62) 
They forgot His deeds and the wonders He had shown them.

(Psalms 78:63) 
He performed miracles in Egypt, His wonders in the plain of Zoan.

(Psalms 78:64) 
He turned their rivers to blood, and they could not drink from their streams.

(Psalms 78:65) 
He sent swarms of flies that devoured them, and frogs that destroyed them.

(Psalms 78:66) 
He gave their crops to the locusts, and the fruit of their labor to the grasshoppers.

(Psalms 78:67) 
He destroyed their vines with hail and their sycamore-fig trees with frost.

(Psalms 78:68) 
He gave their cattle over to the hail, and their flocks to the lightning.

(Psalms 78:69) 
He unleashed against them the heat of His anger, His wrath, indignation, and trouble—a band of destroying angels.

(Psalms 78:70) 
He made a path for His anger; He did not spare their lives from death, but gave their lives over to the plague.

(Psalms 78:71) 
He struck down all the firstborn in Egypt, the firstfruits of their strength in the tents of Ham.

(Psalms 78:72) 
But He led out His people like a flock; He guided them like a flock through the desert.

(Psalms 78:73) 
He led them safely, and they were not afraid, while the sea engulfed their enemies.

(Psalms 78:74) 
He brought them to the border of His holy land, to the mountain His right hand had won.

(Psalms 78:75) 
He drove out the nations before them, and apportioned their land as an inheritance by lot.

(Psalms 78:76) 
He made the tribes of Israel dwell in their tents.

(Psalms 78:77) 
Then He turned away and abandoned them, and did not give them any more help.

(Psalms 78:78) 
So He was angry with Israel, and utterly rejected them.

(Psalms 78:79) 
He abandoned the tabernacle in Shiloh, the tent He had pitched among men.

(Psalms 78:80) 
He allowed His strength to be captured, and His glory to be in the hands of the enemy.

(Psalms 78:81) 
He gave His people over to the sword, and was not concerned about His inheritance.

(Psalms 78:82) 
Fire devoured their young men, and their young women were not praised.

(Psalms 78:83) 
Their priests fell by the sword, and their widows were not lamented.

(Psalms 78:84) 
Then the Lord awoke as if from sleep, like a warrior refreshed by wine.

(Psalms 78:85) 
He struck his enemies in the rear, and put them to everlasting shame.

(Psalms 78:86) 
He rejected the tent of Joseph, and did not choose the tribe of Ephraim;

(Psalms 78:87) 
but He chose the tribe of Judah, Mount Zion, which He loved.

(Psalms 78:88) 
He built His sanctuary like the high heavens, like the earth, which He established forever.

(Psalms 78:89) 
He chose David His servant, and took him from the sheep pens.

(Psalms 78:90) 
From tending the ewes with their young, He brought him to shepherd Jacob His people, Israel His inheritance.

(Psalms 78:91) 
He shepherded them with a pure heart, and guided them with skillful hands.

(Psalms 79:1) 
A Psalm by Asaph. O God, gentiles have entered into your inheritance. They have defiled your holy temple and have made Jerusalem into a pile of rubble.

(Psalms 79:2) 
They left the corpses of your servants as food for the birds in the sky. They left the flesh of your saints for the beasts of the land.

(Psalms 79:3) 
They have shed their blood like water all around Jerusalem, and there was no one who would bury them.

(Psalms 79:4) 
We have become the mockery of our neighbors, a laughingstock and a joke to those around us.

(Psalms 79:5) 
How long, O Lord? Will you be angry forever? Will your jealousy burn like a fire?

(Psalms 79:6) 
Pour out your wrath on the gentiles who do not know you, and on the kingdoms that have not called on your name.

(Psalms 79:7) 
For they have consumed Jacob, and they have laid waste his place.

(Psalms 79:8) 
Do not remember our former iniquities. Let your mercies quickly come to meet us, for we have become very poor.

(Psalms 79:9) 
Help us, O God of our salvation, and for the glory of your name, deliver us. Be gracious to our sins for your name's sake.

(Psalms 79:10) 
Why should the nations say, "Where is their God?" Let the vengeance for the blood of your servants, which has been poured out, be made known among the nations before our eyes.

(Psalms 79:11) 
Let the groaning of the prisoners come before you. According to the greatness of your arm, preserve the sons of death.

(Psalms 79:12) 
And repay our neighbors sevenfold into their bosom the reproach with which they have reproached you, O Lord.

(Psalms 79:13) 
But we, your people, and the sheep of your pasture, will give you thanks forever. We will announce your praise from generation to generation.

(Psalms 80:1) 
For the leader; for the presses. A Psalm. Of Asaph.

(Psalms 80:2) 
O Shepherd of Israel, give ear, You who lead Joseph like a sheep.

(Psalms 80:3) 
You who sit above the cherubim, be revealed.

(Psalms 80:4) 
Before Ephraim, and Benjamin, and Manasseh, stir up Your power, and come to save us.

(Psalms 80:5) 
Turn us back, O God, and show us Your face, and we shall be saved.

(Psalms 80:6) 
O Lord God of hosts, how long will You be angry with Your servant's prayer?

(Psalms 80:7) 
You have fed us with the bread of tears, and given us tears to drink in full measure.

(Psalms 80:8) 
You have made us a source of conflict for our neighbors, and our enemies mock us.

(Psalms 80:9) 
Turn us back, O God of hosts, and show us Your face, and we shall be saved.

(Psalms 80:10) 
You brought a vine out of Egypt; You cast out the nations and planted it.

(Psalms 80:11) 
You were the guide of its journey; You planted its roots, and it filled the earth.

(Psalms 80:12) 
Its shadow covered the mountains, and its branches the cedars of God.

(Psalms 80:13) 
It sent out its branches to the sea, and its shoots to the river.

(Psalms 80:14) 
Why have You broken down its walls, so that all who pass by the way pluck it?

(Psalms 80:15) 
The boar from the forest ravages it, and the wild beast devours it.

(Psalms 80:16) 
Turn, God of hosts! Look down from heaven, and see, and visit this vine.

(Psalms 80:17) 
Protect that which Your right hand has planted, and the son of man whom You have strengthened for Yourself.

(Psalms 80:18) 
It is burned with fire, and cut down at the rebuke of Your countenance.

(Psalms 80:19) 
Let Your hand be upon the man of Your right hand, and upon the son of man whom You have strengthened for Yourself.

(Psalms 80:20) 
Then we will not turn back from You; You will revive us, and we will call upon Your name.

(Psalms 80:21) 
O Lord God of hosts, turn us back; show Your face, and we shall be saved.

(Psalms 81:1) 
For the leader. A song. For the wine presses, the sons of Korah.

(Psalms 81:2) 
How beloved are your tabernacles, Lord of hosts!

(Psalms 81:3) 
My soul longs, and faints, for the courts of the Lord.

(Psalms 81:4) 
My heart and my flesh have rejoiced in the living God.

(Psalms 81:5) 
For even the sparrow has found a house for itself, and the turtledove a nest for itself, where it may lay its young.

(Psalms 81:6) 
Your altars, Lord of hosts, my King and my God!

(Psalms 81:7) 
Blessed are those who dwell in your house, O Lord: they shall praise you for ever and ever.

(Psalms 81:8) 
Blessed is the man whose help comes from you: He has arranged ascensions in his heart.

(Psalms 81:9) 
Passing through the valley of tears, in the place that he has appointed.

(Psalms 81:10) 
For the lawgiver will give a blessing: they shall go from strength to strength: the God of gods will be seen in Sion.

(Psalms 81:11) 
O Lord God of hosts, hear my prayer: give ear, O God of Jacob.

(Psalms 81:12) 
Behold our protector, O God: and look upon the face of your Christ.

(Psalms 81:13) 
For one day in your courts is better than a thousand.

(Psalms 81:14) 
I have chosen to be a castaway in the house of my God, rather than to dwell in the tents of sinners.

(Psalms 81:15) 
For God loves mercy and truth: the Lord will give grace and glory.

(Psalms 81:16) 
He will not deprive of goods those who walk in their innocence.

(Psalms 81:17) 
O Lord God of hosts, blessed is the man who hopes in you.

(Psalms 82:1) 
God has taken His place among the assembly of all the gods, and He judges them all, fairly.

(Psalms 82:2) 
“How much longer will you judge unfairly? How much longer will you favor the wicked?

(Psalms 82:3) 
Judge the needy, the orphan, the humble, and the poor.

(Psalms 82:4) 
Rescue the poor and the weak from the hand of the wicked.

(Psalms 82:5) 
They don't know anything, and they don't understand. They wander in darkness, and they don't know. All the foundations of the earth are shaking.

(Psalms 82:6) 
I said, 'You are gods; you are all sons of the Most High.'

(Psalms 82:7) 
But you will die as mere men do. You'll fall as any prince would.

(Psalms 82:8) 
Arise, God, and judge the earth, for You will inherit all the nations.

(Psalms 83:1) 
The song of Psalm 83 by Asaph.

(Psalms 83:2) 
O God, who is like You? Don't be silent, don't hold back, O God.

(Psalms 83:3) 
Your enemies are rising up, and those who hate You are growing in power.

(Psalms 83:4) 
They conspire against Your people. They plot against those dedicated to You.

(Psalms 83:5) 
They say, “Come, let's destroy them. Let's wipe out their nation so that Israel is forgotten forever.”

(Psalms 83:6) 
They all agree and make an alliance against You,

(Psalms 83:7) 
The tents of Edom, the Ishmaelites, Moab, and the Hagarenes;

(Psalms 83:8) 
Gebal, Ammon, Amalek, Philistia, and the inhabitants of Tyre.

(Psalms 83:9) 
Assyria has also joined them, supporting the descendants of Lot.

(Psalms 83:10) 
Do to them what You did to Midian and Sisera, what You did to Jabin at the Kishon River.

(Psalms 83:11) 
They were defeated at Endor, and they rotted away, polluting the land.

(Psalms 83:12) 
Treat their leaders as You treated Oreb, Zeb, Zeba, and Zalmunna, all of their leaders.

(Psalms 83:13) 
They said, “Let’s take possession of God's territory!”

(Psalms 83:14) 
O my God, make them like a rolling wheel, like chaff before the wind.

(Psalms 83:15) 
As fire consumes a forest, as a flame sets mountains ablaze,

(Psalms 83:16) 
So shall You pursue them with Your storm. In Your wrath, terrify them!

(Psalms 83:17) 
Fill their faces with shame. Then they will seek Your name, O Lord.

(Psalms 83:18) 
May they be ashamed and terrified forever. May they be disgraced and destroyed.

(Psalms 83:19) 
Then they will know that You alone are the Lord. You alone are the Most High over all the earth.

You have calmed all Your wrath; You have turned away from the heat of Your anger.

(Psalms 86:3) 
Have mercy on me, O Lord, for I call to you all day long.

(Psalms 86:4) 
Bring joy to the soul of your servant, because, O Lord, I lift up my soul to you.

(Psalms 86:5) 
For you, Lord, are good and forgiving, abounding in mercy to all who call upon you.

(Psalms 86:6) 
Lord, hear my prayer and listen to my plea.

(Psalms 86:7) 
In the day of my distress, I called to you because you heard me.

(Psalms 86:10) 
For you are great and do marvelous deeds; you alone are God.

(Psalms 86:12)

(Psalms 86:13) 
For your mercy to me is great, and you have rescued my soul from the depths of hell.

(Psalms 86:15) 
But you, Lord God, are compassionate and gracious, slow to anger, abounding in mercy and faithfulness.

(Psalms 86:17)

(Psalms 88:1) 
O Lord, God of my salvation: by day I have cried out, and in the night before you.

(Psalms 88:2) 
Let my prayer enter into your presence: incline your ear to my prayer.

(Psalms 88:3) 
For my soul is filled with evils: and my life has approached to the abyss.

(Psalms 88:4) 
I am counted among those who go down into the pit: I have become like a man without help,

(Psalms 88:5) 
free among the dead: like the wounded sleeping in the sepulchres, of whom you are no longer mindful: and they have been cast off from your hand.

(Psalms 88:6) 
They have laid me in the lowest pit: in darkness, and in the shadow of death.

(Psalms 88:7) 
Your wrath has been confirmed over me: and you have brought all your waves over me.

(Psalms 88:8) 
You have distanced my acquaintances from me: they have made me an abomination to themselves.

(Psalms 88:9) 
I have been delivered, and I could not go out: my eyes languished for want.

(Psalms 88:13) 
Will your wonders be known in the dark, and your justice in the land of oblivion?

(Psalms 88:14) 
And I, O Lord, have cried to you: and in the morning my prayer will come before you.

(Psalms 88:18)

(Psalms 88:19)

(Psalms 90:1) 
Lord, you have been our refuge from one generation to the next.

(Psalms 90:2) 
Even before the mountains were made, before the earth and all the universe were formed, you have always existed, and you will always exist.

(Psalms 90:3) 
You turn men back to dust and say: “Return, sons of men!”

(Psalms 90:4) 
Because a thousand years in your sight are like the passing of yesterday, like a fleeting moment in the night.

(Psalms 90:5) 
You sweep people away in death; their lives are a mere moment. They’re like grass that quickly withers,

(Psalms 90:6) 
that flourishes in the morning, but by evening it is cut down, withered, and dried up.

(Psalms 90:7) 
We are consumed by your anger; we are terrified by your wrath.

(Psalms 90:8) 
You have placed our sins before you, our secret sins under the light of your presence.

(Psalms 90:9) 
All of our days pass under your wrath; we are consumed in a moment.

(Psalms 90:10) 
The years of our lives pass like a spider’s web. The span of our lives is seventy years,

(Psalms 90:11) 
or perhaps, if we are strong, eighty years; even then, their lives are spent mostly in toil and sorrow.

(Psalms 90:12) 
They quickly pass away; we fade.

(Psalms 90:13) 
Who knows the power of your anger? Who understands the full extent of your wrath?

(Psalms 90:14) 
Teach us to number our days so that we may gain a heart of wisdom.

(Psalms 90:15) 
Return, O Lord! How long will you delay? Have pity on your servants.

(Psalms 90:16) 
Satisfy us each morning with your love so that we may be filled with joy for all our days.

(Psalms 90:17) 
Make us rejoice for as long as you have afflicted us, for the years when we saw suffering.

(Psalms 90:18) 
Show your servants your work, and show your glory to their children.

(Psalms 90:19) 
May the Lord, our God, show us his favor. Make all that we do succeed. Yes, make it all succeed.

(Psalms 91:1) 
If you dwell and rest in the help of the Highest God, then you will also dwell in the protection of the sky.

(Psalms 91:2) 
You will say to God the Father: "You are my protector and my refuge: my God, in You I will hope."

(Psalms 91:3) 
Because He freed me from the snare of the hunters and from a harsh word.

(Psalms 91:4) 
With His wings He will overshadow you and protect you, and under His protection you will hope:

(Psalms 91:5) 
His truth and love is a shield and a protection.

(Psalms 91:6) 
You will not fear the fear of the darkness of night, nor will you be frightened by the arrow of sin that flies in the day,

(Psalms 91:7) 
nor of the plague that travels in darkness, nor of the destruction and the devil of the midday sun.

(Psalms 91:8) 
Though a thousand men may fall at your side, and ten thousand at your right hand:

(Psalms 91:9) 
it will not come near you.

(Psalms 91:10) 
But your eyes will see what the true nature of things are, and you will see the punishment of sinners.

(Psalms 91:11) 
Because you are, O Lord, my hope:

(Psalms 91:12) 
You have made God the Highest, your refuge.

(Psalms 91:13) 
Evil shall not come to you, and the scourge of sin will not come near your dwelling.

(Psalms 91:14) 
For He has given His angels the command to guard you in all your ways.

(Psalms 91:15) 
They will carry you in their hands, so you will not strike your foot against a stone.

(Psalms 91:16) 
You will walk over the asp and the basilisk: and you will trample on the lion and the dragon.

(Psalms 91:17) 
“Because he has hoped in Me, I will free him, and I will protect him, because he knows My Name.

(Psalms 91:18) 
When he calls to Me, I will hear him: I am with him in tribulation: I will rescue him, and I will glorify him.

(Psalms 91:19) 
I will fill him with length of days, and I will show him My salvation.

(Psalms 92:1) 
This is a Psalm for singing on the Sabbath.

(Psalms 92:2) 
It is right to give praise to God; and to sing hymns to your name, Most High God;

(Psalms 92:3) 
Proclaiming Your mercy in the morning, and Your truth through the night:

(Psalms 92:4) 
With a ten-stringed instrument, with a hymn on the harp.

(Psalms 92:5) 
For You have made me glad, O Lord, by Your works: and in the works of Your hands I will rejoice.

(Psalms 92:6) 
How great are Your works, O Lord! Your thoughts are exceedingly deep.

(Psalms 92:7) 
The foolish man does not know this, and the stupid man does not understand.

(Psalms 92:8) 
When the wicked spring up like grass, and all those who work iniquity have appeared,

(Psalms 92:9) 
They will perish forever. But you, O Lord, are most high forever.

(Psalms 92:10) 
For behold, Your enemies, O Lord, for behold, Your enemies will perish: and all who work iniquity will be scattered.

(Psalms 92:11) 
And my horn will be exalted like that of a unicorn: and my old age will abound in mercy.

(Psalms 92:12) 
My eye has looked down on my enemies, and my ear has heard the wicked who rise up against me.

(Psalms 92:13) 
The righteous will flourish like a palm tree: and will grow like the cedar of Lebanon.

(Psalms 92:14) 
Planted in the house of the Lord, they will flourish in the courts of our God.

(Psalms 92:15) 
They will still multiply in old age: and will be prosperous, that they may announce.

(Psalms 92:16) 
For the Lord our God is just: and there is no iniquity in Him.

(Psalms 93:1) 
The Lord is reigning. He is wearing majestic glory.

(Psalms 93:2) 
The Lord has put on strength and is always ready.

(Psalms 93:3) 
Indeed, He has established the Earth itself so that it will not be moved.

(Psalms 93:4) 
Your throne was established long ago: From eternity, You are.

(Psalms 93:5) 
The floods have lifted up, O Lord. The floods have lifted their voices.

(Psalms 93:6) 
The floods have lifted up their waves, louder than the sound of rushing waters.

(Psalms 93:7) 
More wonderful than the waves of the sea; The Lord in the heavens is to be admired.

(Psalms 93:8) 
Your testimonies are completely trustworthy. Holiness is fitting for your house, O Lord, forever and ever.

(Psalms 94:1) 
The God of vengeance is the Lord, and He will right all wrongs.

(Psalms 94:2) 
He will raise Himself up to judge the earth, and He will give every arrogant person what they deserve.

(Psalms 94:3) 
Lord, how much longer will the wicked sin? How much longer will the wicked be honored?

(Psalms 94:4) 
They are always saying evil things, and they are always saying them.

(Psalms 94:5) 
Lord, they are crushing your people, and they are tormenting your inheritance.

(Psalms 94:6) 
They murder widows and foreigners, and they kill orphans.

(Psalms 94:7) 
They say, “The Lord will not see it, and the God of Jacob will not understand.”

(Psalms 94:8) 
Understand this, foolish people. You fools, wake up!

(Psalms 94:9) 
God made our ears, and He will hear us. God made our eyes, and He will see us.

(Psalms 94:10) 
God teaches knowledge to man and will correct the nations. 

(Psalms 94:11) 
The Lord knows the thoughts of men, that they are vain.

(Psalms 94:12) 
Happy is the man whom the Lord corrects; He will teach him out of His law.

(Psalms 94:13) 
God will give him rest from the evil days until the pit is dug for the wicked man.

(Psalms 94:14) 
Because the Lord will not forsake His people, nor will He abandon His inheritance.

(Psalms 94:15) 
Until justice comes back to the righteous, those who follow it will be right.

(Psalms 94:16) 
Who will stand up with me against the wicked? Who will take a stand with me against the evildoers?

(Psalms 94:17) 
If the Lord had not helped me, my soul would have already been in the realm of the dead.

(Psalms 94:18) 
If I said, “My foot is slipping,” your mercy, Lord, was helping me.

(Psalms 94:19) 
When I was distressed, your consolations gave joy to my soul.

(Psalms 94:20) 
Is your seat a seat of wickedness? Do you make trouble with your commandments?

(Psalms 94:21) 
They hunt for the soul of the righteous and condemn innocent blood.

(Psalms 94:22) 
But the Lord has become my refuge; and my God is a help to my hope.

(Psalms 94:23) 
God will give them back what they deserve, and in their wickedness, He will destroy them, the Lord our God.

(Psalms 95:3)

(Psalms 95:4) 
Because the Lord is great, and worthy of very great praise: He is terrifying above all the false gods.

(Psalms 95:5) 
For all the gods of the Gentiles are demons: but the Lord created the sky.

(Psalms 95:6) 
Majesty and beauty are in His sight: holiness and greatness are in His sanctification.

(Psalms 95:7)

(Psalms 95:8) 
offer the Lord the glory of His name: adore the Lord in His holy courtyard.

(Psalms 95:9) 
Tremble before Him, all the earth: say among the nations that the Lord reigns.

(Psalms 95:10) 
For He has established the world and it will not be moved: He will judge the peoples in righteousness.

(Psalms 95:11) 
Let the skies rejoice, and let the earth exult: let the sea and its fullness be moved.

(Psalms 95:12) 
The fields will exult, and everything that is in them: then all the trees of the forests will exult

(Psalms 95:13) 
before the face of the Lord: because He comes, because He comes to judge the earth. He will judge the world in justice, and the peoples in His truth.

(Psalms 101:1) 
Lord, hear my prayer, and let my cry come to you.

(Psalms 101:2) 
Don't turn your face away from me; on whatever day I am troubled, incline your ear to me.

(Psalms 101:3) 
On whatever day I call upon you, quickly hear me.

(Psalms 101:4) 
Because my days have vanished like smoke, and my bones have dried up like a fire's ash.

(Psalms 101:5) 
I am struck like grass, and my heart has withered, because I have forgotten to eat my bread.

(Psalms 101:6) 
Because of the voice of my groaning, my bone has clung to my flesh.

(Psalms 101:7) 
I have become like a pelican in the wilderness; I am like a night raven in a dwelling.

(Psalms 101:8) 
I have watched and become like a solitary sparrow on a roof.

(Psalms 101:9) 
All day my enemies reproached me, and those who praised me swore against me.

(Psalms 101:10) 
Because I ate ash as my bread, and I mixed my drink with weeping.

(Psalms 101:11) 
Because of your anger and indignation, because you raised me up and cast me down.

(Psalms 101:12) 
My days have declined like a shadow, and I have dried up like grass.

(Psalms 101:13) 
But you, Lord, remain forever, and your memory endures to all generations.

(Psalms 101:14) 
You will arise, and have mercy on Zion; for the time to have mercy on it has come, because the time has come.

(Psalms 101:15) 
For your servants have found pleasure in her stones, and they will have mercy on her lands.

(Psalms 101:16) 
And the nations will fear the name of the Lord, and all the kings of the earth will fear your glory.

(Psalms 101:17) 
Because the Lord has built up Zion, and he will be seen in his glory.

(Psalms 101:18) 
He has regarded the prayer of the humble, and he has not despised their prayer.

(Psalms 101:19) 
Let this be written for the next generation, and the people who are being created will praise the Lord.

(Psalms 101:20) 
Because he has looked down from his holy height, the Lord looked from heaven to the earth:

(Psalms 101:21) 
To hear the groaning of those in chains, to release the sons of those slain:

(Psalms 101:22) 
That they may declare in Zion the name of the Lord, and his praise in Jerusalem.

(Psalms 101:23) 
When peoples come together, and kings to serve the Lord.

(Psalms 101:24)

(Psalms 101:25) 
Do not take me away in the middle of my days. Your years are generation after generation.

(Psalms 101:26) 
In the beginning, Lord, you founded the earth, and the heavens are the work of your hands.

(Psalms 101:27) 
They will perish, but you will remain, and all things will grow old like a garment.

(Psalms 101:28)

(Psalms 101:29)

He forgives all your iniquities; He heals all your illnesses.

(Psalms 102:4) 
He redeems your life from destruction; He crowns you with mercy and compassion.

(Psalms 102:5) 
He fills your desire with good things, so that your youth is renewed like the eagle's.

(Psalms 102:6) 
The Lord does acts of mercy and justice for all who are wronged.

(Psalms 102:7) 
He made known His ways to Moses, and His will to the children of Israel.

(Psalms 102:8) 
The Lord is compassionate and merciful, slow to anger and abounding in mercy.

(Psalms 102:9) 
He will not always be angry, nor will He keep His anger forever.

(Psalms 102:10) 
He has not dealt with us according to our sins, nor has He repaid us according to our iniquities.

(Psalms 102:12) 
As far as the east is from the west, so far has He removed our transgressions from us.

(Psalms 102:14)

(Psalms 102:17)

(Psalms 102:18)

(Psalms 102:19)

(Psalms 104:1) 
Praise God, my soul!

(Psalms 104:2) 
You are truly magnificent, my Lord God.

(Psalms 104:3) 
You have robed yourself with majesty and beauty.

(Psalms 104:4) 
You are clothed in light as if with a garment.

(Psalms 104:5) 
You spread out the sky like a tent.

(Psalms 104:6) 
You build your home above the sky; your high dwelling is in the heavens.

(Psalms 104:7) 
You make the clouds your chariot,

(Psalms 104:8) 
You travel on the wings of the wind.

(Psalms 104:9) 
You make the winds your messengers,

(Psalms 104:10) 
and flaming fire your servants.

(Psalms 104:11) 
You set the earth on its foundations

(Psalms 104:12) 
so that it shall never be moved.

(Psalms 104:13) 
You covered it with the deep as with a garment;

(Psalms 104:14) 
the waters stood above the mountains.

(Psalms 104:15) 
At your rebuke they fled,

(Psalms 104:16) 
at the voice of your thunder they hastened away.

(Psalms 104:17) 
They rose up to the mountains, they went down into the valleys

(Psalms 104:18) 
to the place which you established for them.

(Psalms 104:19) 
You set a boundary which they shall not pass,

(Psalms 104:20) 
neither shall they return to cover the earth.

(Psalms 104:21) 
You cause springs to gush forth in the valleys;

(Psalms 104:22) 
they flow between the mountains.

(Psalms 104:23) 
They give drink to every beast of the field;

(Psalms 104:24) 
the wild asses quench their thirst.

(Psalms 104:25) 
Beside them the birds of the heavens dwell;

(Psalms 104:26) 
they sing among the branches.

(Psalms 104:27) 
From your lofty abode you water the mountains;

(Psalms 104:28) 
the earth is satisfied with the fruit of your works.

(Psalms 104:29) 
You cause the grass to grow for the cattle,

(Psalms 104:30) 
and plants for the service of man,

(Psalms 104:31) 
that you may bring forth food from the earth,

(Psalms 104:32) 
and wine to gladden the heart of man,

(Psalms 104:33) 
to make his face shine with oil,

(Psalms 104:34) 
and bread to strengthen man's heart.

(Psalms 104:35) 
The trees of the Lord are watered abundantly, the cedars of Lebanon, which he planted.

(Psalms 104:36) 
There the birds build their nests;

(Psalms 104:37) 
the stork has its home there.

(Psalms 104:38) 
The high mountains are for the wild goats;

(Psalms 104:39) 
the rocks are a refuge for the rock badgers.

(Psalms 104:40) 
You have made the moon to mark the seasons;

(Psalms 104:41) 
the sun knows its time for setting.

(Psalms 104:42) 
You make darkness, and it is night,

(Psalms 104:43) 
when all the beasts of the forest move about.

(Psalms 104:44) 
The young lions roar for their prey, seeking their food from God.

(Psalms 104:45) 
When the sun rises, they go away,

(Psalms 104:46) 
and lie down in their dens.

(Psalms 104:47) 
Man goes forth to his work

(Psalms 104:48) 
and to his labor until the evening.

(Psalms 104:49) 
How manifold are your works, O Lord!

(Psalms 104:50) 
In wisdom you have made them all;

(Psalms 104:51) 
the earth is full of your creatures.

(Psalms 104:52) 
Here is the sea, great and wide,

(Psalms 104:53) 
which teems with things innumerable,

(Psalms 104:54) 
living things both small and great.

(Psalms 104:55) 
There go the ships,

(Psalms 104:56) 
and Leviathan, which you formed to sport in it.

(Psalms 104:57) 
These all look to you, to give them their food in due season.

(Psalms 104:58) 
When you give to them, they gather it up; when you open your hand, they are filled with good things.

(Psalms 104:59) 
When you hide your face, they are dismayed;

(Psalms 104:60) 
when you take away their breath, they die and return to their dust.

(Psalms 104:61) 
When you send forth your spirit, they are created,

(Psalms 104:62) 
and you renew the face of the ground.

(Psalms 105:1) 
Praise the Lord, call on his name: announce among the nations his works.

(Psalms 105:2) 
Sing to him, and sing songs to him: tell all his marvelous acts.

(Psalms 105:3) 
Praise his holy name: let the heart of those who seek the Lord rejoice.

(Psalms 105:4) 
Seek the Lord and be made strong: always seek his face.

(Psalms 105:5) 
Remember the marvels he has made: his wonders, and the judgments of his mouth.

(Psalms 105:6) 
Offspring of Abraham, his servant: sons of Jacob, his chosen ones.

(Psalms 105:7) 
He is the Lord our God: his judgments are in all the earth.

(Psalms 105:8) 
He has remembered his covenant forever: the word he commanded to a thousand generations.

(Psalms 105:9) 
Which he arranged for Abraham: and his oath to Isaac:

(Psalms 105:10) 
And he established it for Jacob as a precept: and for Israel as an everlasting testament:

(Psalms 105:11) 
Saying: “To you I will give the land of Canaan: the measuring cord of your inheritance.”

(Psalms 105:12) 
When they were few in number: the fewest, and inhabitants of it:

(Psalms 105:13) 
And they passed from nation to nation, and from one kingdom to another people.

(Psalms 105:14) 
He did not let any man hurt them: and he rebuked kings for them.

(Psalms 105:15) 
Do not touch my anointed ones: and do not mistreat my prophets.

(Psalms 105:16) 
And he called a famine upon the land: and he broke all the support of bread.

(Psalms 105:17) 
He sent a man before them: Joseph was sold as a slave.

(Psalms 105:18) 
They humbled his feet in chains: iron passed through his soul.

(Psalms 105:19) 
Until his word came: the word of the Lord set him ablaze.

(Psalms 105:20) 
He sent and released him: the king of the peoples set him free.

(Psalms 105:21) 
He established him as lord of his house: and prince over all his possessions:

(Psalms 105:22) 
That he might teach his princes like himself: and his elders wisdom.

(Psalms 105:23) 
And Israel entered Egypt: and Jacob was a sojourner in the land of Ham.

(Psalms 105:24) 
And he greatly increased his people: and made them stronger than their enemies.

(Psalms 105:25) 
He turned their heart to hate his people: and to deal deceitfully with his servants.

(Psalms 105:26) 
He sent Moses his servant: Aaron whom he chose for himself.

(Psalms 105:27) 
They placed among them the words of his signs: and his signs in the land of Ham.

(Psalms 105:28) 
He sent darkness, and it was darkened: and he did not exacerbate his words.

(Psalms 105:29) 
He turned their waters into blood: and killed their fish.

(Psalms 105:30) 
Their land brought forth frogs: in the inner chambers of their kings.

(Psalms 105:31) 
He spoke, and there came gnats: and gnats in all their borders.

(Psalms 105:32) 
He gave them hail for rain: fire burning in their land.

(Psalms 105:33) 
And he struck their vines and their fig trees: and broke the wood of their borders.

(Psalms 105:34) 
He spoke, and the locust came, and the caterpillar: of which there was no number.

(Psalms 105:35) 
And it ate every blade of grass in their land: and ate every fruit of their land.

(Psalms 105:36) 
And he struck every firstborn in their land: the first fruits of all their labor.

(Psalms 105:37) 
And he led them out with silver and gold: and not one weak person was among their tribes.

(Psalms 105:38) 
Egypt rejoiced in their departure: because the fear of them had fallen upon them.

(Psalms 105:39) 
He spread a cloud for their protection: and a fire to light them at night.

(Psalms 105:40) 
They asked, and the quail came: and he satisfied them with bread from the sky.

(Psalms 105:41) 
He split the rock, and waters flowed: in the desert: and they went out like rivers.

(Psalms 105:42) 
Because he remembered his holy word: which he spoke to Abraham his servant.

(Psalms 105:43) 
And he led out his people with exultation: and his chosen ones with joy.

(Psalms 105:44) 
And he gave them the lands of the nations: and they possessed the labors of the peoples:

(Psalms 105:45) 
That they might keep his ordinances: and seek his law.

(Psalms 105:46) 
Amen.

(Psalms 106:1) 
Give thanks to God, because He is good, because His mercy endures forever.

(Psalms 106:2) 
Let those who were saved by God declare it! He saved them from the hands of the enemy.

(Psalms 106:3) 
He gathered them from the ends of the earth, from the east and the west, the north and the sea.

(Psalms 106:4) 
They wandered in the desert, lost, without a way to reach a city where they could be safe.

(Psalms 106:5) 
They were hungry and thirsty, and their life nearly failed within them.

(Psalms 106:6) 
But they cried out to God in their distress, and He saved them from their troubles.

(Psalms 106:7) 
Then He led them on the right path, so that they could find the city where they could live.

(Psalms 106:8) 
Let them thank God for His mercy and for the wonders He does for all people:

(Psalms 106:9) 
He satisfies the thirsty and the hungry.

(Psalms 106:10) 
Some sat in darkness, bound in poverty and chains.

(Psalms 106:11) 
They rejected God's word and rejected the plan of the Most High.

(Psalms 106:12)

(Psalms 106:13) 
But they cried out to God in their distress, and He saved them from their troubles.

(Psalms 106:14) 
He brought them out of darkness and the shadow of death, and broke their chains.

(Psalms 106:15) 
Let them thank God for His mercy and for the wonders He does for all people:

(Psalms 106:16) 
He shattered the bronze gates, and broke the iron bars.

(Psalms 106:17)

(Psalms 106:18) 
They abhorred all food, and came close to the gates of death.

(Psalms 106:19) 
But they cried out to God in their distress, and He saved them from their troubles.

(Psalms 106:20) 
He sent out His word and healed them, saving them from destruction.

(Psalms 106:21) 
Let them thank God for His mercy and for the wonders He does for all people:

(Psalms 106:22)

(Psalms 106:23) 
Some sail the sea in ships, doing business on the great waters,

(Psalms 106:24) 
They saw God's works, and His wonders in the deep.

(Psalms 106:25) 
He commanded, and a stormy wind arose, lifting up the waves.

(Psalms 106:26) 
They were tossed up to the sky, and plunged down to the depths; their souls melted away in their troubles.

(Psalms 106:27) 
They reeled and staggered like a drunken man, and all their wisdom was consumed.

(Psalms 106:28) 
Then they cried out to God in their distress, and He brought them out of their troubles.

(Psalms 106:29) 
He stilled the storm and caused the waves to cease.

(Psalms 106:30) 
They rejoiced because it was calm, and He led them to the harbor they desired.

(Psalms 106:31) 
Let them thank God for His mercy and for the wonders He does for all people:

(Psalms 106:32) 
Let them exalt Him in the assembly of the people, and praise Him in the council of the elders.

(Psalms 106:33) 
He turned rivers into a desert and springs of water into thirst.

(Psalms 106:34) 
He turned fertile land into a salt waste, because of the wickedness of those who live there.

(Psalms 106:35) 
He turned the desert into a pool of water, and a dry land into springs of water.

(Psalms 106:36) 
And there He let the hungry dwell, and they founded a city to live in.

(Psalms 106:37) 
They sowed fields, planted vineyards, and reaped a fruitful harvest.

(Psalms 106:38) 
He blessed them and they multiplied greatly, and He did not decrease their livestock.

(Psalms 106:39) 
But then they were few, and oppressed by trouble and sorrow.

(Psalms 106:40) 
He poured contempt upon princes, and caused them to wander in a pathless waste.

(Psalms 106:41) 
But He lifted up the poor and needy out of their suffering.

(Psalms 106:42) 
The righteous saw and rejoiced, and all wickedness closed its mouth.

(Psalms 106:43)

(Psalms 108:1) 
A hymn of David. O God, keep singing my praises, and do not be silent: for the mouth of the sinner, and the mouth of the deceitful, is opened against me.

(Psalms 108:2) 
With a lying tongue, they spoke against me, and with words of hatred, they surrounded me: and they fought against me for nothing.

(Psalms 108:3) 
For their love of me, they slandered me: but I prayed.

(Psalms 108:4) 
And they repaid me with evil for good, and hatred for my love.

(Psalms 108:5) 
Appoint a sinner against him, and let the devil stand at his right hand.

(Psalms 108:6) 
When he is judged, let him be condemned: and let his prayer become sin.

(Psalms 108:7) 
Let his days be few: and let another receive his office.

(Psalms 108:8) 
Let his children be orphans, and his wife a widow.

(Psalms 108:9) 
Let his sons be transferred, and beg: let them be cast out of their habitations.

(Psalms 108:10) 
Let the usurer search out all his substance: and let strangers plunder his labors.

(Psalms 108:11) 
Let there be no one to help him: nor let there be anyone to pity his orphans.

(Psalms 108:12) 
Let his children be devoted to destruction: in one generation let his name be blotted out.

(Psalms 108:13) 
Let the iniquity of his fathers be remembered before the Lord: and let not the sin of his mother be blotted out.

(Psalms 108:14) 
Let them be always against the Lord: and let the memory of them perish from the earth.

(Psalms 108:15) 
Because he did not remember to show mercy, but persecuted the poor man and the beggar, and broke the heart of the afflicted until death.

(Psalms 108:16) 
And he loved cursing, and it will come to him: and he did not want blessing, and it will be far from him.

(Psalms 108:17) 
And he put on cursing as a garment: and it entered like water into his inner self, and like oil into his bones.

(Psalms 108:18) 
May it be to him like the garment with which he is covered, and like the belt with which he is always girded.

(Psalms 108:19) 
This is the work of those who detract from me before the Lord, and who speak evil against my soul.

(Psalms 108:20) 
But you, O Lord, O Lord, deal with me for your name's sake: because your mercy is sweet.

(Psalms 108:21) 
Deliver me, because I am needy and poor: and my heart is troubled within me.

(Psalms 108:22) 
I have been taken away like a shadow when it is extended: and I have been shaken off like locusts.

(Psalms 108:23) 
My knees have been weakened by fasting: and my flesh has been changed because of oil.

(Psalms 108:24) 
And I have become a reproach to them: they saw me, and shook their heads.

(Psalms 108:25) 
Help me, O Lord my God: save me according to your mercy.

(Psalms 108:26) 
And let them know that this is your hand: and you, O Lord, have done it.

(Psalms 108:27) 
Let them curse, but you bless: let those who rise up against me be confounded: but your servant will rejoice.

(Psalms 108:28) 
Let those who detract from me be clothed with shame: and let them be covered as with a double cloak of their own confusion.

(Psalms 108:29) 
I will give thanks greatly to the Lord with my mouth: and I will praise him in the midst of many.

(Psalms 108:30) 
Because he has stood at the right hand of the poor: to save my soul from those who persecute me.

I will make your enemies into the footstool of your throne.”

The Lord will send forth your royal scepter from Zion, and you will rule in the midst of your enemies.

(Psalms 109:4) 
You are a priest forever, with all of your royal glory. You are radiant with divine holiness; You were born before the morning star.

(Psalms 109:5) 
The Lord has sworn an oath, and He will not change his mind, “You are a priest forever, just like Melchizedek.”

(Psalms 109:6) 
The Lord is at your right hand, crushing kings on the day of His wrath.

(Psalms 109:7) 
He will pass judgment on the nations and He will bring an end to wickedness. He will shatter the heads of the wicked all over the earth.

(Psalms 109:8) 
The Son drinks from the stream along the way; so He will raise up His head.

(Psalms 110:6) 
The Lord is at your right hand; he has broken kings in the day of his wrath.

(Psalms 110:7)

He will drink from the brook beside the way; therefore he will lift up his head.

I love God because He hears the voice of my prayers.

The terrors of death surrounded me. The dangers of the grave came upon me.

(Psalms 116:4) 
I found myself in trouble and sorrow, so I called upon the name of the Lord.
